They may get angry with the infant, causing the child to become unruly; or they may drink while nursing, causing the child to become frightened and suffer fits; or while pregnant and nursing, leading the child to become jaundiced and emaciated; or they may suffer from illnesses, causing the child to have convulsions and unusual ailments; or they may vomit after nursing, resulting in the child vomiting and becoming thin; or they may overfeed the child, leading to excessive heat and rapid breathing; or they may be unsteady in their duties as wet nurses, causing the child to become ill; or the wet nurse sleeping with the child, where the breath from their mouths and noses affects the child's nose, leading to nasal congestion; or excessive maternal affection leading to tightly bound clothing, which causes additional coldness and excess heat, resulting in the child suffering from fevers, wind toxins, and skin diseases. Additionally, there are situations where the wet nurse leaves the child’s clothing under the moonlight to dry overnight, where droppings from birds fall on the clothes, thus resulting in unfortunate diseases; or if they play with strange objects that frighten the child when seen suddenly, leading to shock. The Book states: "Clothes laid under the moon invite unwarranted calamities; children, not fully formed, may suffer from contact with rare objects." All these are due to the mother’s mistakes, causing the child to lose essence and blood, leading to a darkened complexion and weakened limbs, ultimately contributing to illness and death. Thus, the Inner Canon does not record any discourse on the diseases of infants being nursed; those serious ailments are unfounded.[19p]

中古巫妨氏着《颅顖经》以占寿夭，历世相授，于是小儿医方兴焉。其次晋宋江左推诸苏家小儿方传习有验，隋间有巢氏方撰集《病源》，唐有孙真人留心此术。迨后贤俊俊集，名医颇众。然小儿治法，散在诸书。博考群书论说，但有证而无治法。张焕有方而阙脉证，惟钱氏一书，古今所重。谓小儿方脉，固难求证，不可以言语取者，乳下之婴，襁褓之孩，故专于一科。古人有言医之为难而兹幼科，比诸医者，又出人一头地。虽然人有长幼，病感则一，但幼小不能言者耳。人有四百四证，能调则生，失和则死。[20p]

In the Middle Ages, the Wu Fang clan composed the "Lú Hán Jing" to predict longevity and mortality, passing it down through generations. Thus, pediatric medicine began to flourish. Following this, during the Jin and Song dynasties, various medical practices from the Su family were transmitted with proven efficacy in Jiangnan. In the Sui dynasty, the Chao family compiled the "Bing Yuan," while in the Tang dynasty, Master Sun paid special attention to this field. Eventually, many talented physicians emerged, and renowned doctors became numerous. However, pediatric treatments are scattered across various texts. Despite extensive research on numerous writings, methods of treatment are often absent, offering only evidence without practical approaches. Zhang Huan provided formulas but lacked information on pulse diagnosis, while only the works of the Qian family are esteemed by both ancient and modern practitioners. It is said that the pulse of children is inherently difficult to verify and cannot be defined merely by language, particularly for infants and small children. Therefore, it focuses on one specific discipline. Ancients remarked on the difficulty of medicine, and in this pediatric field, practitioners can be significantly more advanced than general physicians. Although individuals vary in age, their ailments are similar, yet young children cannot express themselves. There are four hundred forty forms of diseases, and if one can adjust them, life is sustained; if harmony is lost, death ensues.[20p]

幼者归罪于母，壮者或四气七情，或饥饱劳逸，或嗜欲误犯，皆能成疾。故上古神农氏之王天下也，观人之违和，啜草木之味，以定咸酸甘苦，以治疾病沉疴。咸以软之，酸以收之，甘以缓之，苦以坚之。奇哉辛味，总摄四性。然后播种百谷，以养人之形骸。古考巢居穴处，不昧其道，故能全形返质，以道自守，气血坚刚。终保百年之寿。于是乎明医间出，继踵不绝。岐和振袂于前，李华驰声于后。悲哉，后人巧伪日增，故此夭寿不满。虽有明医续世，诊视无功。淫祀妖邪，以求余福，可谓息灯觅朗，枯壑驾舟，虽欲求生，反遭艰险。大抵养生之士，要识违和之理，则天命无穷矣。[21p]

The young blame their mothers, while the grown may suffer due to the four seasons and seven emotions, or from hunger, fullness, labor, and rest, or from desires leading to errors, all of which can result in illness. In ancient times, when the divine farmer ruled the world, he observed people's disharmony and tasted the flavors of plants to determine salty, sour, sweet, and bitter, in order to treat diseases and chronic ailments. Salt softened, sourness astringed, sweetness eased, and bitterness strengthened. Remarkably, the pungent flavor encompassed all four qualities. He then sowed a hundred grains to nourish the human body. Ancient practices of residing in nests or caves did not obscure their path, allowing them to maintain their form and return to essence, guarding themselves through the Way, with strong and resilient vital energy and blood. Thus, they could preserve their lives for a hundred years. Consequently, skilled physicians emerged in succession without end. Qi and He were prominent at the forefront, while Li and Hua made their names known afterward. Alas, in modern times, deception and craftiness have increased, resulting in premature deaths. Even with enlightened physicians continuing through the ages, their diagnoses often bring little effect. Engaging in excessive rituals and seeking false blessings is like trying to find brightness in the dark or rowing a boat through a dry ravine; though one desires to live, they encounter dangers instead. Ultimately, those who seek to sustain life must understand the principles of harmony and discord, for then the mandate of heaven is boundless.[21p]

　　　　片玉心书 【明　万全】

　　　　　指南赋

　　小儿方术号曰哑科。口不能言，脉无可施。惟形色以为凭，竭心思而调治。故善养子者，似豢龙以调护；不善养子者，如舐犊而爱惜。爱之愈勤，害之愈急。乍头温而足冷，忽多啼而不乳。差之毫厘，失之千里。肠胃脆薄兮，饮食易伤；筋骨柔弱兮，风寒易袭。父母何知，看承太弛。重绵厚袄，反助阳以耗阴；流歠放饭，徒败脾而损胃。闻异声，见异物，失于堤防；深其居，简其出，过于周密。未期而行立兮，喜其长成；无事而嬉笑兮，谓之聪慧。一旦病生，双亲心戚。不信医而信巫，罔求药而求鬼。乃人事之不修，谓天命之如此。[22p]

A Heartfelt Letter on the Refinement of Nature

On the Guidance of Raising Children

The art of raising children is often called the "Mute Discipline." When they cannot speak and pulses show no signs, we can only rely on their physical appearance for guidance. Thus, those who are good at nurturing children treat them as they would a nurturing dragon; while those who are poor at it do so as one would pet a calf with affection. The more care you provide, the greater the harm can become. At times, a child’s head may be warm while their feet are cold; they may cry often but refuse to feed. A slight deviation can lead to significant missteps. Their intestines and stomach are delicate, easily harmed by food; their muscles and bones are weak, easily affected by wind and cold. What do parents know, as they cling to the notion of tradition? Heavy blankets and thick clothing may inadvertently consume the yang energy while exhausting the yin; careless feeding and overflow of food only ruin the spleen and damage the stomach. Unfamiliar sounds and sights may lead to carelessness; one may confine a child too much within the home while limiting their outings excessively. Premature attempts to make them stand are taken as signs of growth; laughing and playing without purpose is mistaken for cleverness. Yet, once illness strikes, the parents are filled with anxiety. They trust shamans over doctors, seeking spirits rather than remedies. Such failures in human responsibility are mistakenly attributed to fate.[22p]

　　　　育婴家秘 【明　万全】

　　　　　发微赋

　　医道至博，幼科最难。如草之芽兮，贵于调养；似蚕之苗兮，慎于保全。血气未充兮，脉无可诊；神识未开兮，口不能言。诚求于心，详察于面。苟得其要也，握造化于妙手；未达其旨也，摘章句于残编。调护若失，疾病乃生。头要凉而背要暖，食勿饱而衣勿绵。肠胃脆薄兮，乳哺伤而成积；精神怯弱兮，闻见异而成癎。嗟哉慈母兮，过于姑息；笑彼粗工兮，误于汤丸。伐其发生之气，夭其童稚之年。徒啼号于丘垄，休祷祀于旃坛。
　　　　　小儿不宜妄针灸

　　芽儿嫩小不耐伤，针灸汤丸莫妄尝。破肉损筋成瘦疾，坏肠败胃作余殃。　　初生小儿，内外脆薄，药石针灸，必不能耐也。良工当以爱己子之心，而爱人之子，怜惜之，抚摩之，未可轻治，为儿作祸也。书曰：如保赤子，其爱养之谓欤。为父母者，不可不知。[23p]

Secrets of Infant Care
(Ming Dynasty, Wan Quan)

A Poem on Subtlety

The art of medicine is vast, yet pediatrics is the most challenging. Like the tender sprout, it thrives on careful nurturing; like the silkworm’s shoot, it requires cautious preservation. When blood and energy have not yet filled them, their pulses cannot be diagnosed; when their awareness has not yet awakened, their mouths cannot articulate. Truly seeking in one’s heart, observing closely on the surface. If one grasps the essentials, they can wield transformation in skilled hands; if one fails to understand the intent, they merely extract phrases from fragmented texts. If care is misplaced, illness will arise. The head must be kept cool while the back needs warmth, food should not be plentiful and clothing should not be too soft. The intestines and stomach are delicate; overfeeding can lead to accumulation; if the spirit is timid and frail, strange sights and sounds can induce spasms. Alas, kind mother, you are too indulgent; laughing at those who are clumsy, you err with ineffective remedies. Sapping the essence of growth, you stifle the years of youth. Merely wailing in the fields, cease worship at the altars.

Children Should Not Be Recklessly Treated with Acupuncture

Tender buds cannot endure harm; do not recklessly try acupuncture or remedies. Breaking flesh and damaging tendons lead to thinness and illness; spoiling intestines and harming stomachs cause lasting misfortunes. Newly born infants are fragile inside and out; they certainly cannot tolerate medicinal stones or acupuncture. Good practitioners should care for others' children as they would their own, treating them gently, caressing them; do not take light actions to avoid causing misfortune. The text states: "To protect the infant is to nurture it with love." Parents must bear this in mind.[23p]

　　　　　鞠养以慎其疾

　　小儿神气衰弱，忽见非常之物，或见未识之人，或闻鸡鸣犬吠，或见牛马禽兽，嬉戏惊吓，或闻人之叫呼，雷霆铳爆之声，未有不惊动者也，皆成客忤惊癎之病。盖心藏神，惊则伤神；肾藏志，恐则志失。大人皆然，小儿为甚也。凡小儿嬉戏，不可妄指他物作虫作蛇；小儿啼哭，不可令装扮欺诈以止其啼，使神志昏乱，心小胆怯成客忤也。不可不慎。　　小儿玩弄嬉戏，常在目前之物，不可去之。但勿使之弄刀剑，衔铜钱，近水火，见鬼神耳。　　小儿能言，必教之以正言，如鄙俚之言勿语也。能食则教以恭敬，如亵慢之习勿作也。能坐能行则扶持之，勿使倾跌也。宗族乡党之人，则教以亲疏尊卑长幼之分，勿使谍嫚。[24p]

Care for them by being cautious of their fears

Young children are naturally weak in spirit. They may suddenly encounter unusual sights, unfamiliar people, sounds of roosters crowing or dogs barking, or see cattle and horses, and be startled or frightened by playful activities. They might hear calls and shouts from others, or the thunderous sounds of explosions, and it is impossible for them not to be disturbed, leading to illness due to fright. The heart stores the spirit, and fright damages the spirit; the kidneys store will, and fear causes loss of will. This holds true for all adults, but is even more pronounced in children. When children are playing, they must not be allowed to recklessly point at objects and imagine them to be insects or snakes. If a child cries, they should not be deceived by disguises to stop their crying, as it can confuse their spirit, making them timid and fearful. One must be cautious.

Children should play with things within reach; these should not be taken away from them. However, they must not be allowed to handle knives or swords, carry money, or be near water or fire, and they should not see spirits or ghosts.

When children begin to speak, they should be taught proper language and not be allowed to use vulgar expressions. If they can eat, they should be taught to do so respectfully, avoiding rudeness. If they can sit or walk, they should be supported to prevent falls. Relatives and community members should teach them to understand the distinctions of kinship, respect, and the hierarchy of age and seniors, ensuring they do not behave disdainfully.[24p]

言语问答，教以诚实，勿使欺妄也。宾客教以拜揖迎送，勿使退避也。衣服器用五谷六畜之类，遇物则教之，使其知之也。或教以数目，或教以方隅，或教以岁月时日之类。如此则不但无疾，而知识亦早也。　　小儿周岁有病者，勿妄用药，调其乳母可也。不得已而用，必中病之药，病衰则已，勿过其则也。　　幼科有拿掐法者，乃按摩之变也。以小儿未周岁者，难以药饵治，权宜之则，可以治外邪，而不能治内病也。能治小疾及气实者，如大病气虚者用之，必误儿也。为父母喜拿而恶药，致令夭折者，是谁之过欤？　　父母常将幼子怜，几因爱恤取愁烦。育婴家秘无多术，要受三分饥与寒。　　人之无子者，置姬妾，觅方术，问命卜，祷鬼神，其心劳矣。[25p]

In verbal exchanges, teach honesty, and do not allow deceit to arise. In hosting guests, teach how to bow and greet, and do not permit them to withdraw. When it comes to clothing, tools, grains, and livestock, when encountering these matters, provide instruction so they come to understand. Teach them numbers, measurements, and the passage of days and seasons. Thus, not only will there be no illness, but knowledge will flourish early.

For children who are a year old and ill, do not recklessly use medicines; instead, adjust their nurse. If absolutely necessary to use medicine, it must be the correct one for the illness. Once the symptoms lessen, do not exceed the prescribed treatment.

In pediatrics, there are methods involving pinching; this is a variation of massage. For infants under a year old, it is difficult to treat them with medicine. Only those practices that address external ailments may be suitable; they cannot cure internal diseases. Treating minor ailments or excessive energy as if they were serious or deficient conditions will surely harm the child. What blame lies with parents who delight in pinching but detest medicines, leading to premature death?

Parents often cherish their young children, but sometimes love can turn into worry and distress. Caring for infants involves few secret methods; one must endure a measure of hunger and cold.

Those without children may seek concubines, search for remedies, consult diviners, and pray to deities, yet their hearts are troubled.[25p]

及其生子，爱恤之深，保养之失，过于热也，热则生风，过于饱，饱则成积。医不择良药，或犯毒不可救也。柳子《种木传》云：虽曰爱之，其实害之。所以取譬也。　　谚云：若要小儿安，常受三分饥与寒。饥谓节其饮食也，寒谓适其寒温也，勿令太饱太暖之意，非不食不衣之谬说也。　　头要清凉背要温，露其下体养真阴。天时勿犯如春候，寒热乖违客气侵。　　此言适其寒温之法也。头者六阳之会，常要凉，不可缠裹。腹为阴，背为阳，皆脏腑之俞膜也，常要和暖，不可便露。小儿纯阳之气，嫌于无阴，故下体要露，使近地气以养其阴也。天时者，即寒热也。春者温和之气，万物皆赖以生长也。谓襁褓之中，寒不犯寒，热不犯热，常如春气温和时，以长养儿之身体。[26p]

When a child is born, the depth of love and care can lead to neglect in their upbringing. If the care is excessive, it can create a hot environment; if they are overfed, it can lead to accumulation. A physician cannot choose an excellent remedy, as sometimes a harmful poison cannot be saved from. Liu Zhi in "The Transmission of Growing Trees" states that although it is said to love, in reality, it can cause harm. This is taken as a metaphor.

A saying goes: If you want a child to be peaceful, they should often experience a bit of hunger and cold. Hunger refers to moderating their diet, while cold means adapting to a suitable temperature, implying they should not be too full or too warm; this is not an erroneous claim of not feeding or not clothing.

The head should be kept cool and the back warm, exposing the lower body to nurture the true yin. One should not violate the seasons; during spring, cold and heat should not conflict with the body’s natural conditions.

This describes the method of adjusting temperature. The head is where the six yang energies converge and must remain cool, not bundled up. The abdomen represents yin and the back represents yang; both should be warm and protected from exposure. A child's pure yang energy lacks yin, so the lower body should be exposed to connect with the earth’s energy to nourish their yin. The seasons also refer to cold and heat. Spring represents a gentle and warm atmosphere, which all living things rely on for growth. This means that in swaddling, cold should not harm the cold, and heat should not harm the heat, so that the child can grow in a pleasant and mild environment like that of spring.[26p]

若有乖违，寒热之客气来侵矣。　　乳为血化美如饧，肉谷虽甘更乱真。到得后来能食日，莫教纵恣损脾阴。　　此言节其饮食之法也。儿在母腹之时，赖血以番。既生之后，饮食之乳，亦血之所化也。虽有谷肉，不可与之，以乱其肠胃中和之气。至于能食，尤当节之，不可纵其所好，以快其心，因而致病者多矣。《内经》曰：饮食自倍，肠胃乃伤。不可不慎也。　　耳目之神寄在心，异闻异见易生惊。痰生气逆因成癎，恨煞终身作废人。　　乳母须求不病人，择其体厚性和平。不贪口腹无淫欲，鞠养何求子不成。　　养子之道当择乳母，必取无病妇人，肌肉丰肥，性情和平者为之，则其乳汁浓厚甘美，莹白温和，于子有益。如病寒者乳寒，病疮者乳毒，贪口腹者则味不纯，喜淫欲者则气不清，何益于子？故宜远之。[27p]

If there are deviations, the invasion of cold and hot energies will come. Milk transforms into blood, beautiful like syrup; though meat and grains are delicious, they disturb the true essence. When it comes to eating, one should not indulge in excess and harm the spleen and yin. This refers to the principle of moderation in diet. While a child is in the womb, it relies on blood for nourishment. Once born, the milk, also transformed from blood, is vital. Although grains and meats exist, they should not be given, as they would disturb the harmony in the stomach and intestines. When able to eat, moderation is even more essential, for indulging in desires to please the heart can lead to illness. The Inner Canon states: excessive eating harms the stomach and intestines. One must be cautious.

The spirits of the ears and eyes reside in the heart, and unusual sights and sounds can easily provoke fear. Phlegm arises from counterflow of qi and can result in convulsions, causing lifelong regret and leading to a wasted life.

A wet-nurse must be chosen from healthy women, selecting those who are strong and of balanced temperament. One should not be greedy for food or indulge in desires, for how can one expect a child to thrive under such conditions?

The path of nurturing a child requires selecting a wet-nurse who is certainly healthy, with rich and abundant flesh, and a gentle temperament, as her milk will be thick, sweet, pure, and warm, benefiting the child. If the wet-nurse is cold, her milk will be cold; if she has sores, her milk will be toxic; if she is greedy, the taste will not be pure; if she indulges in desires, the qi will not be clear. What benefit can this bring to the child? Thus, it is advisable to stay away from such individuals.[27p]

　　　　幼科发挥 【明　万全】

　　　　　治未病

　　脐在两肾之间，任冲胃三脉之所系也。儿之初生，断脐护脐，不可不慎。故断脐之时，隔衣咬断者，上也；以火燎而断之，次也；以剪断之，以火烙之，又其次也。护脐之法：脐既断矣，用软布缠裹，待干自落，勿使犯水也。三朝洗儿，当护其脐，勿使水渍入也。脐落之后，皆换包裙，勿使尿湿浸及脐中也。如此调护，则无脐风之病。所谓上工治未病，十得十全也。　　小儿病有三：因衣太厚则热，太薄则冷，冷热之伤，此外因也。乳多则饱，乳少则饥，饥饱之伤，内因也。客忤中恶，坠仆折伤，此不内不外因也。顺乎天时，适其寒温，则不伤冷伤热矣。慎择乳母，节其饮食，则不伤饥饱矣。调护之法，爱惜之深，必无纵弛之失矣。慎勿使庸医妄用汤丸，误儿性命。[28p]

Preventing Illness Before It Emerges

The navel is situated between the two kidneys, connecting to the three vessels of the stomach. Upon a child's birth, the cutting and care of the navel must be done with extreme caution. Therefore, at the time of cutting the navel, doing it through clothing is the best method; cutting it with fire is the next best; using scissors and then cauterizing it is the least favorable.

For the care of the navel: once it is cut, wrap it in a soft cloth and allow it to fall off naturally when dry; avoid getting it wet. During the three days after birth, when washing the baby, take care to keep water from touching the navel. After the navel has fallen, change the swaddling cloth frequently to prevent urine from wetting it. By following this careful approach, one can avoid the condition known as "navel wind." The so-called expert treats illnesses before they arise, achieving perfect success.

Children's ailments can be attributed to three main causes: clothing that is too thick causes overheating, while clothing that is too thin leads to chill; these are external factors. If there is too much milk, the child feels full; if there is too little, the child feels hungry; these variations are internal causes. Additionally, external factors such as being affected by evil influences or falling and getting hurt also contribute to illness.

By aligning with the seasonal weather and adjusting to its warmth or cold, one can avoid issues arising from temperature extremes. Careful selection of a wet nurse and regulating her diet help prevent any problems associated with hunger and fullness. Care and attention in nursing are essential to avoid neglect. Be especially cautious not to allow incompetent doctors to recklessly administer medications, as it may harm the child's life.[28p]

　　　　婴童百问 【明　鲁伯嗣】

　　　　　初诞

　　婴童在胎，禀阴阳五行之气，以生成五腑六脏。百骸之体悉具，必借胎液以滋养之，受气既足，自然分娩。初离母体，口有液毒，啼声未出，急用软绵裹指，拭去口中恶汁，虽是良法，然仓卒之际，或有不及如法者。古人有黄连法、朱蜜法、甘草法，用之殊佳。免使恶物咽下，伏之于心，遇天行时气，久热不除，乃乘于心，心主血脉，得热而散，流溢于胃，而胃主肌肉，发出于外。故成疮疹之候。世之长幼，无有可免者。若依初生拭口之法，得免痘疹之患。或有时气侵染，只出肤疮细疹，易为调理，亦孩童之幸也。杨氏云：初生拭口不前，恶秽入腹，则腹满气短，不能饮乳者，宜用茯苓丸加减治之。又法：下胎毒，临产落草时，浓煎淡豉汁服，极好，不可与辰砂、黄连、轻粉等。[29p]

Infant's Hundred Questions (Ming Dynasty, Ru Boxi)

Birth

When an infant is in the womb, it receives the energies of Yin and Yang and the Five Elements, thus forming the Five Visceral Organs and Six Bowels. The entire body is fully developed, and it must rely on amniotic fluid for nourishment. Once the qi is sufficient, natural birth follows. Upon leaving the mother's body, the infant may have toxic fluids in the mouth and may not cry immediately, so it is essential to quickly use soft cloth to wipe away the foul juices from the mouth. Although this is a good method, in hurried situations, some may not do it properly. The ancients had methods involving huanglian (Coptis), zhumi (honey), and licorice, which are particularly effective. This prevents the ingestion of harmful substances that settle in the heart. When exposed to seasonal ailments, if such toxins persist due to warmth, they can spread through the bloodstream, overflow into the stomach, and since the stomach governs muscle, this may manifest as sores and rashes. No one, young or old, can escape this. If one follows the method of wiping the mouth at birth, they may avoid the affliction of pox and rashes. Sometimes, if seasonal illnesses invade, only superficial skin ailments manifest, which can be easily managed—this is indeed fortunate for the child. Yang said: if the mouth is not wiped at birth and impurities enter the stomach, this can lead to abdominal fullness and shortness of breath, preventing the infant from breastfeeding; in such cases, one should use a modified formula with Poria pills for treatment. Moreover, to expel fetal toxins during labor, drinking a concentrated decoction of light fermented soybean juice is excellent, but one must avoid substances like cinnabar, huanglian, and light powder.[29p]

　　　　　护养法

　　小儿始生，肌肤未实，不可暖衣，止当薄衣，但令背暖。薄衣之法，当从秋习之，不可以春夏卒减其衣，否则令中风寒。所以从秋习之者，以渐稍寒。如此则必耐寒。冬月但着两薄襦可耐寒，若不忍见其寒，当略加耳。若爱而暖之，适所以害之也。又当消息，无令出汗。如汗出则表虚，风邪易入也。昼夜寤寐。常当慎之。其哺乳之法，亦当有节，不可过饱。或宿滞不化，当用消乳丸化积温脾等剂治之。陈氏所谓：忍三分寒，吃七分饱，频揉肚，少洗澡，及要背暖肚暖足暖，要头凉心胸凉，亦至论也。[30p]

Nurturing Method

When a baby is newly born, their skin is not yet firm, and they should not be dressed in warm clothing. Only thin clothing should be used, ensuring the back is kept warm. This thin clothing method should be adopted from autumn; one must not abruptly reduce clothing in spring or summer, as this could invite wind and cold. Thus, following the adaptation from autumn allows for gradual acclimatization to cold. In winter, wearing two thin garments is sufficient to endure the cold; if it feels too cold, a slight addition is acceptable. However, if one excessively warms them out of love, it may actually be harmful.

Moreover, one must pay attention to the baby's condition, ensuring they do not sweat. If sweating occurs, it indicates a weakness on the surface, making them susceptible to external wind evil. Whether awake or asleep, one should always be cautious. The breastfeeding method should also be regulated to avoid overfeeding. If there is stagnation and inability to digest, one should use breast milk pills or other remedies to transform accumulated heat and strengthen the spleen. As Chen states: endure a slight chill, eat moderately, rub the belly frequently, bathe infrequently, and ensure the back, belly, and feet are warm while keeping the head and chest cool; this advice holds true.[30p]

　　　　医学正传 【明　虞抟】

　　　　　小儿初生食饮

　　小儿受患，其为母者，胎前既不能谨节，胎后又不能调护，是以惟务姑息，不能防微杜渐。或未满百晬而遂与酸咸之味，或未彀周岁而辄与肥甘之物，百病由是而生焉。曰吐泻、曰黄疸、曰五疳、曰腹胀、曰水肿、曰疟、曰痢、曰痰喘，岂非吃食过伤，调善失宜之所致欤？
　　　　保婴金镜录 【明　薛己】

　　　　　论初生用药

　　愚谓凡小儿在月内外者，调补之剂，每服亦不过二三匙。若表散攻伐之药，则每服只可匙许而已，过多则反伤元气。余当量大小虚宜加减。若乳母之疾，致儿为患，当治母为主，子少服之。后仿此。
　　　　保婴撮要 【明　薛铠】[31p]

On Infant Feeding and Illness

When infants suffer, their mothers are to blame. Before birth, they fail to be cautious with their diet; after birth, they are unable to provide proper care. Hence, they only seek to indulge the child, neglecting to prevent minor issues from becoming significant problems. Some children are given sour or salty foods before they reach the age of one hundred days, or rich and fatty foods before they are even a year old, leading to various illnesses: vomiting, diarrhea, jaundice, malnutrition, abdominal swelling, edema, malaria, dysentery, and wheezing. Are these not the results of excessive eating and inappropriate dietary adjustments?

On Medication for Newborns

I foolishly suggest that for infants within the first month or so, tonic medicines should be administered in doses of two to three spoonfuls. For dispersing or attacking medicines, only a spoonful should be given at a time; too much will harm their vital energy. Dosages should be adjusted according to the size and condition of the child. If the mother is ill and it affects the child, the focus should be on treating the mother, and the child should receive minimal medication. Later treatments should follow this principle.[31p]

　　　　　初诞法

　　小儿分娩之时，口含血块，须急于未啼时，用软帛裹指，穵去其血，用黄连、豆豉、朱、蜜、甘草解之。但黄连性寒，若禀母气膏粱积热者，宜服；若滋味淡薄胎气元弱者，又不宜用。其朱砂固能解毒，恐金石镇坠，不若只以牛黄分许，蜜调与吮为佳。世多用犀角解毒丸，其胎气虚寒虚弱者，反伤脾胃生气，甚至不育。又有婴儿因其难产，或冒风寒而垂危者，切不可便断脐带，急烘绵絮，包抱怀中，急以胎衣置火中煨烧，更以火纸捻于脐带上往来燎之，使暖气入腹，须臾气复自苏。尤戒洗浴，恐脉理不密，元气发泄，而外邪乘之也。
　　　　　护养法

　　小儿初生，须令乳母预慎七情六淫，厚味炙煿，则乳汁清宁，儿不致疾。否则阴阳偏胜，血气沸腾，乳汁败坏，必生诸证。若屡用药饵，则脏腑阴损，多变败证，可不慎欤。大抵保婴之法，未病则调治乳母，既病则审治婴儿，亦必兼治其母为善。[32p]

Method of Initial Birth

When a child is born, if they have blood clots in their mouth, it is crucial to clean this before they cry. Use a soft cloth wrapped around the finger to wipe away the blood, and then administer a mixture of Huang Lian (Coptis), Dou Chi (Fermented Soybeans), Zhusha (Cinnabar), honey, and licorice to detoxify. However, Huang Lian is cold in nature; if the mother has consumed rich foods that generate heat, it is appropriate to use it. Conversely, if the child is weak and has a bland constitution, it is not advisable. While Zhusha can effectively detoxify, it has a tendency to anchor one down, so it is better to use Niuhuang (Cattle Gallstone) in moderation mixed with honey for sucking. Many in the world use Xijiao (Rhinoceros Horn) detoxification pills, but for those with weak and cold vital energy, these can harm the spleen and stomach, potentially leading to infertility. Additionally, if an infant suffers from a difficult birth or is exposed to wind and cold, the umbilical cord should not be cut hastily. Quickly warm cotton and cradle the child, placing the placental tissue over fire to gently heat, and apply burning paper around the umbilical cord to bring warmth into the abdomen, allowing the vital energy to recover swiftly. Bathing should especially be avoided, as it may disrupt the pulse and lead to the escape of the original qi, making the child susceptible to external pathogens.

Method of Nurturing

Upon birth, it is essential for the wet nurse to be cautious about emotional disturbances and rich flavors. If the milk is pure and calm, the child will be healthy. Otherwise, imbalances in yin and yang can lead to turbulent blood and qi, spoiling the milk, which will surely result in various ailments. Frequent use of medications may harm the internal organs and lead to serious complications that should not be overlooked. Generally, the method of caring for infants is to adjust and care for the wet nurse when the child is healthy and to carefully treat the infant when they are unwell, always ensuring the mother is also treated effectively.[32p]

　　　　医学纲目 【明、楼英】

　　　　　初生禁忌

　　田式曰：大凡小儿过暖生热，热极生风，提抱生痈，喂饲生癖，最宜慎之。　　钱氏曰：大喜后食乳食，多成惊癎；大哭后食乳食，多成吐泻。
　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

　　　　　婴幼论

　　王隐君曰：凡婴儿六十日后，瞳人将成，而能应和人情。自此为有识之初，便当诱其正性，父母尊长，渐次令其别之。僮仆婢妾，不可训其手舞足蹈，无礼骂人，高举放倒，猛推闪避，儿虽强笑，失色惊骇，乖张恶性，自此无端。乳母纵嗜厚味纯醪煎煿，儿亦受之于乳，是以惊疳积癖泻痢由之而生。及其临病，又忌灌以苦辛之药味。姑息隐忍，无所不至。大抵爱子之偏，无出于母，所嗜之食，任其饱足，以致所伤。余幼时酷嗜甘饴，忽于一日甘饴中有蚯蚓引头而出，自此不敢食饴。至长始知长上为之。不然，脾疳久患，深染难调，奈何不为戕害。[33p]

Medical Guidelines: Initial Restrictions

Tian Shi says: Generally, when infants are too warm, it causes heat; excessive heat leads to wind; holding them excessively results in sores; feeding them improperly leads to afflictions. Caution is especially necessary. Qian explains: Feeding milk after great joy often leads to convulsions; feeding milk after intense crying often causes vomiting and diarrhea.

Ancient and Modern Medical Treatises

Wang Yinjun states: For infants, after sixty days, their pupils begin to form, and they can start responding to human emotions. From this onset of recognition, parents and elders should gradually guide them in appropriate behavior. Servants and maids should not be allowed to train the child in mock dances, disrespect, shouting, or rough pushing and dodging. Even if the child appears to smile, they may be frightened and distressed, leading to an unruly temperament. If a wet nurse indulges in rich flavors and strong alcoholic essences, the infant also absorbs this through milk, resulting in various ailments. When sick, they should avoid bitter and spicy medications. Indulgence and tolerance can lead to serious issues. The mother's affection, often excessive, manifests in the food she craves, allowing the child to overindulge, leading to harm. In my childhood, I had a strong taste for sweet confections, but one day I discovered a worm emerging from a sweet treat, after which I could not bring myself to eat sweets. Only upon growing up did I understand the reasons for such caution. If not, persistent ailments will deepen and become difficult to remedy, causing irreparable harm.[33p]

　　　　　护养

　　《千金》论曰：小儿二百四十日掌骨成，母当教以匍匐。一周满，母当扶以行步。此皆则法。若或暖衣重围，不见风日，不着地气，致令筋骨软弱，数岁不能行者有之。今观田舍小儿则反是，所以见风日得土气，筋力常健，岂贵贱之理有异哉。明乎此，则保婴之道得矣。
　　　　　乳哺

　　乳哺之法，不可不慎。小儿脾胃怯弱，乳食易伤。初得作呕泻，久则成积癖。乳母饮食，乳汁便通；儿食其乳，所感立应。母食热则乳热，母食寒则乳寒。夏食热乳则致吐逆，冬食寒乳则致嗽利。母不欲怒，怒则气上为狂；母不欲醉，醉则身热腹痛。怀孕乳儿，致令黄瘦，腹大脚软，名曰鬾病。大都乳哺不可太过。谚云：小儿常病伤于饱也。又曰：忍三分饥，吃七分饱。亦至论也。[34p]

Nurturing

The text from "Thousand Gold" states: A child's bones form after two hundred forty days, so the mother should teach them to crawl. By the end of a week, the mother should support them to walk. This is all proper training. If one were to dress them in heavy clothing, keep them from sunlight and fresh air, preventing contact with the earth, it could lead to weak muscles and bones, causing some children to be unable to walk for years. Observing children in rural areas reveals the opposite; they benefit from exposure to sunlight and fresh air, keeping their muscles strong. Isn't this principle independent of wealth or status? Understanding this leads to the proper methods of child-rearing.

Breastfeeding

The methods of breastfeeding must be approached with caution. Infants have weak spleens and stomachs, and are easily harmed by food. Initial vomiting and diarrhea can cause long-term digestive issues. The diet of the wet nurse affects the breast milk; if she eats hot food, the milk becomes hot; if she eats cold food, the milk becomes cold. Consuming hot milk in summer can cause vomiting, while cold milk in winter may lead to cough and diarrhea. The mother should avoid anger; anger raises her Qi and causes chaos; she should avoid drunkenness as well, since it creates heat and abdomen pain. During pregnancy and while nursing, if care is not taken, it can lead to a yellowish and emaciated appearance, with a swollen abdomen and soft feet, referred to as "bile disease." Generally, breastfeeding should not be excessive. A saying goes: "Children often fall ill from overeating." It is also advised: "Endure a little hunger, eat until seven parts full." This is indeed a wise principle.[34p]

　　　　　除胎毒

　　方书皆云：小儿一出腹，啼声未发之时，急用绵裹指，拭去口内恶汁，固是良法，而仓卒之际，或有不及者，故有黄连、甘草、朱、蜜等法用之殊佳。东垣云：只须淡豆豉一味煎汤，与三五口，其毒自下，又能助胃气也，尤妙。
　　　　　初生总论

　　初生小儿，必忌外客所触，古人一岁之内忌之者，并无客忤之患。小儿略识人物，不宜携至神庙，观望神像闪烁，恐生恐惧。　　小儿将入夏时，用色帛缝囊盛去皮尖杏仁七个，与小儿随身佩之，闻雷自然不惊。
　　　　　猪乳法

　　张焕论云：初生时或未有奶子，产妇之乳未下，可用猪乳代之，可免惊癎痘疮。　　钱氏曰：初生小儿至满月内，可常取猪乳滴口中最佳。按《圣惠方》取猪乳，须令猪儿饮母，次便提猪母后脚起，猪儿口自离乳，急用手捋之，即得乳矣，非此法不可取也。[35p]

Elimination of Fetal Toxins

The medical texts all state: When a newborn emerges from the womb and before it cries out, one should quickly use cotton to wipe away the foul fluid from its mouth. This is indeed a good practice; however, in urgent situations, there may be times one cannot do this. Thus, methods using ingredients like Coptis, licorice, vermilion, honey, etc., can be especially beneficial. Dongyuan says: Simply brew a decoction of light fermented soybean and give it to the child, three to five mouthfuls. The toxins will be expelled naturally, and it can also help with the stomach energy, which is particularly wonderful.

General Discussion on Newborns

For newborns, it is essential to avoid contact with outsiders. The ancients believed that for the first year of life, children should not be exposed to guests to prevent any undue harm. Children who can recognize people should not be taken to temples to view the flickering images of deities, as this may instill fear. As summer approaches, sew seven peeled apricot kernels into a sachet for the child to carry with them, which will help them remain calm during thunder.

Use of Pig's Milk

Zhang Huan argues: At birth, if the mother has not yet produced milk, pig's milk can be used as a substitute, preventing seizures, itchy skin, and pox. Qian's theory states: For newborns up to a month old, it is best to frequently give them droplets of pig's milk. According to the "Senghui Formulas," to obtain pig's milk, the piglet must first be allowed to suckle from its mother. Then, one should lift the hind legs of the sow so that the piglet releases its latch. Quickly squeeze out the milk by hand; this is the only proper method to obtain it.[35p]

　　　　　沐浴法

　　小儿洗浴，不可先断脐带，候洗了方断，不致水湿伤脐，可免脐风脐疮等证。用清油调发灰傅脐。洗儿不可用水打湿脐带。
　　　　　断脐法

　　大抵儿初生断脐之后，宜用熟艾厚裹爱护。若乳母不谨，或因洗浴水入脐中，或遗尿在裙抱之内，湿气伤于脐中，或因解脱为风冷邪气所侵，皆能令儿脐肿多啼，不能乳哺，即成脐风也。
　　　　　着衣法

　　《圣惠》论曰：小儿一期之内造衣服，皆须用故帛为之，不可用新绵。若用新绵，则令儿壮热，或作惊癎。
　　　　　晒衣法

　　大抵儿衣日晒夜收，不可露天过夜，次早与儿穿上，致染湿热，使儿不安。此则所谓八邪之害，久则令儿黄瘦腹痛，身上壮热，夜间啼哭，或生疮疥。世俗谓之无辜疾，谓其衣在露天过夜，染着无辜鸟屎，令儿致疾，故曰无辜疾，其实非理。先哲所谓八邪之害，则温热风寒惊积饥饱是也。[36p]

Bathing Method

For infants, the umbilical cord should not be cut before bathing; it should be cut afterward to prevent water from wetting the stump, which could avoid issues like umbilical wind and sores. Use clean oil mixed with ash to protect the umbilical area. Do not let water get the umbilical cord wet during bathing.

Umbilical Cord Cutting Method

Generally, after the umbilical cord is cut at birth, it should be wrapped in moxa for protection. If the wet nurse is not careful, or if bathing water gets into the cord, or if urine is trapped in the wraps, moisture can injure the cord. Furthermore, exposure to cold and wet air can lead to the infant’s cord swelling and excessive crying, preventing them from breastfeeding, which results in umbilical wind.

Clothing Method

According to the "Shenghui," clothing for infants within the first month should be made from old fabric and not from new cotton. If new cotton is used, it may cause the infant to become overheated or lead to seizures.

Clothing Drying Method

Generally, infants’ clothes should be dried in the sun during the day and taken inside at night; they should not be left outdoors overnight. Wearing clothes that have been exposed to dew can cause dampness and heat, making the infant uncomfortable. This is known as the harm of the Eight Evils, which if prolonged, can lead to jaundice, weight loss, abdominal pain, excessive heat at night, crying, or the development of sores or scabs. Commonly, people refer to these conditions as "innocent illnesses," attributing them to clothes left outside overnight accumulating harmful substances, but this is misguided. The ancients referred to the Eight Evils as being influenced by warmth, cold, fright, and imbalanced feeding.[36p]

　　　　　养子日用法

　　吃热吃软吃少则不病，吃冷吃硬吃多则多病。忍三分寒，吃七分饱。频揉肚，少洗澡。　　歌曰：四时欲得小儿安，常要三分饥与寒。但愿人皆依此法，自然诸病不相干。
　　　　　养子十法

　　一要背暖。经云：背脊三椎下节之两旁，是肺之俞也。若风寒伤于肺俞，使人毫毛毕直，皮肤闭而为病热。其证或咳嗽，或喘或呕哕或吐逆，及胸满增寒壮热，皆肺经着寒而得之也。故要背暖。　　二要肚暖。俗云：肚无热肚。肚者胃也，马水谷之海，若冷则物不腐化，肠呜腹痛呕哕泄泻等疾生焉。经云：胃热而能消谷，必能饮食，故要肚暖。　　三要足暖。经曰：足为阳明胃经所司。寒从下起，故要足暖。　　四要头凉。经曰：头者六阳之会，诸阳所凑也。[37p]

Methods for Raising Children

Eating hot, soft, and in moderation prevents illness; eating cold, hard, and in excess leads to sickness. Endure a bit of cold, eat until moderately full. Frequently rub the abdomen, and bathe less. A verse says: To keep children safe through the seasons, maintain a state of slight hunger and chill. If everyone follows this method, naturally, illnesses will not concern them.

Ten Principles for Raising Children

  1. Keep the back warm. The classics say: The two sides below the third vertebra of the back correspond to the lungs. If wind and cold harm the lung area, it causes the hair to stand upright, skin to close, resulting in heat-related illnesses. Symptoms may include cough, shortness of breath, nausea, or chest fullness with cold and heat, all from cold affecting the lung meridian. Therefore, keep the back warm.

  2. Keep the abdomen warm. There is a saying: A cold belly means a cold stomach. The abdomen is the stomach, the sea of water and grains. If cold, food will not digest, leading to abdominal pain, nausea, and diarrhea. The classics say: A warm stomach can digest grains; thus, keep the abdomen warm.

  3. Keep the feet warm. The classics state: The feet govern the yangming stomach meridian. Cold arises from below, so the feet must be warm.

  4. Keep the head cool. The classics say: The head is where the six yang converge and gather all yang energy.[37p]

头为髓之海，若大热则髓溢汗泄，或颅顖肿起，或头缝开解，或头疮目疾。俗云：头无凉头。故头宜凉。　　五要心胸凉。心属丙火，若外受客热，内接心火，则内外俱热也。其证轻则口干舌燥，腮红面赤，重则啼叫惊跳。故心宜凉。　　六者，精神未全，小儿忽见非常之物，或见未识之人，或闻鸡鸣犬吠，忽见牛马等畜，或嬉戏惊骇，或忽闻大声因而作搐者，缘心气成虚而精神离散故也。当用补心益气药治之。如用镇心朱砂、牛黄、琥珀、金、银、脑、麝、水银等药，则成慢惊风搐，以致腹胀足冷，不能疗也。　　七者，不温脾胃，致成吐泻慢惊。[38p]

The head is the sea of marrow; if exposed to great heat, the marrow overflows, leading to sweating and leakage. This can cause swelling of the skull, openings in the sutures, or sores and eye ailments. It is commonly said that "the head cannot be too cool." Therefore, the head should be kept cool.

Next, the heart and chest must also be kept cool. The heart is associated with fire; if it encounters external heat while internal heart fire is present, both inside and outside will become hot. If the symptoms are mild, there may be dry mouth and parched tongue, flushed cheeks, and a reddened face. If severe, there may be crying, agitation, and jumping. Thus, the heart should be kept cool.

Furthermore, if the spirit is not whole, young children may suddenly see something extraordinary, an unfamiliar person, or hear the crowing of a rooster or barking of a dog. They might unexpectedly see cattle or horses, play in fear, or suddenly hear loud noises, leading to involuntary responses. This happens due to a deficiency in the heart's qi, causing the spirit to disperse. It is advisable to use tonifying heart and qi medicines for treatment. However, if using sedative medicines such as cinnabar, gallstone, amber, gold, silver, brains, musk, or mercury, this could lead to chronic wind seizures, resulting in abdominal distension and cold feet, making treatment ineffective.

Lastly, if the spleen and stomach are not kept warm, it can lead to vomiting, diarrhea, and chronic seizures.[38p]

经曰：脾为黄婆，胃为金公，主养五脏六腑。若脾胃全固，则津液通行，气血流畅，表里冲和，一身康健。盖脾胃属土而恶湿。小儿变蒸，上唇肿而头热，或上气身热。父母不晓，妄作伤风伤食治之，或以表药出汗，或以通药宣泄，或以凉药镇心，或以帛汤展缴，致令冷热不调，内伤脾胃，搏于大肠，故粪便青色。久不已者必吐，吐不已者作搐。搐作又言热则生风，转用凉药治之，愈觉败伤真气，渐不救者多矣。经云：脾土虚弱，肝木乘之。故筋挛而作搐，宜用补脾温胃畅气之药治之，庶可得痊也。[39p]

The classics say: The spleen is the Yellow Mother, and the stomach is the Golden Father, responsible for nourishing the five organs and six bowels. If the spleen and stomach are fully solid, then fluids circulate freely, and qi and blood flow smoothly, creating harmony between the exterior and interior, resulting in overall health. The spleen and stomach belong to the earth element and are averse to dampness.

If children develop fever, with swollen upper lips and a hot head, or exhibit heat and agitation, and the parents are unaware, they may mistakenly treat it as a cold or food injury, employing exterior herbs to induce sweating, using purgatives to expel, or cooling herbs to calm the heart, or applying balmy decoctions to alleviate symptoms. This leads to an imbalance of heat and cold, causing internal damage to the spleen and stomach, which may affect the large intestine, resulting in greenish stools. If this persists, vomiting is inevitable, and continued vomiting can lead to convulsions.

Convulsions, characterized by heat, are treated with cooling herbs. However, this can further undermine the true qi, leading to a situation where recovery is increasingly difficult. The classics state: If the spleen and earth are weak, the liver and wood will dominate. Hence, muscle spasms occur, necessitating the use of herbs to tonify the spleen, warm the stomach, and smooth the qi for treatment, so that recovery may be attained.[39p]

　　八者，儿哭未定，勿使饮乳，致儿呕奶粪青，小儿在胎之时，其母取凉过度，冷气入于胞胎之中。儿生之后，因悲啼未定，便与乳食，使气与食蓄结于中，久而不散，致伤脾胃，轻则呕奶粪青，重则腹中气鸣气逆，涎潮流溢，以致难治。　　九者，勿得轻服轻粉、朱砂。夫水银、轻粉俱有毒，虽云下痰，性冷损心气。辰砂虽镇坠，性寒损神，小儿服之易伤，每每被其误也多矣。　　十者，因浴致生丹毒。小儿一周之内，不可轻易频洗，肌肤脆嫩，腠理不密，洗之，恐湿热之气郁蒸不散，变生赤游丹毒，片片如胭脂，身发壮热，若毒气入腹者死。又有因浴伤寒，咳嗽上气，外感之疾，多由此也。[40p]

  1. When the infant is still unsettled from crying, do not let them drink milk, as it can lead to vomiting of greenish milk and feces. When the child is in the womb, if the mother excessively takes in cool air, it will cause coldness to invade the fetus. After the child is born, if they cry in sadness and are immediately given milk, the combination of air and food can become trapped inside, leading to damage to the spleen and stomach. This may result in mild symptoms such as vomiting greenish milk and feces; in severe cases, it can lead to gurgling noises in the abdomen, reversed airflow, and excessive saliva, making it difficult to treat.

  2. Do not lightly administer calamine or cinnabar. Both mercury and calamine are toxic; although they are said to expel phlegm, their nature is cold and harmful to the heart’s energy. Cinnabar, while it can settle anxieties, is also cold and harms the spirit; it is easy to injure young children when they consume it, and many misfortunes arise from this.

  3. Bathing can lead to the development of rashes. Infants within the first week should not be bathed frequently or carelessly, as their skin is delicate and their pores are not tightly closed. Bathing them may trap humid and heated air inside, leading to the emergence of rashes that appear like rouge, resulting in high body temperatures; if toxins penetrate the abdomen, it can be fatal. Additionally, bathing can cause harm that leads to cold symptoms, coughing, and respiratory distress, which often arises from this practice.[40p]

　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

　　　　　小儿论

　　初生儿出月，必须人襁褓。襁褓之道，必须得宜。如春夏之月，乃万物生长之时，宜教令地卧，使之不逆生长之气；如秋冬之月，乃万物收藏之时，宜就温暖之处，使之不逆收藏之气。然后血凝气和，则百病无自而入矣。[41p]

Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment 【Ming Dynasty, Wang Kentang】

On Infants

Newborns should be swaddled for the first month. The method of swaddling must be appropriate. During the spring and summer months, when all things grow, they should be laid on the ground to receive the beneficial growth energy; during the autumn and winter months, when all things are stored, they should be placed in warm areas to avoid counteracting the storing energy. Only then, when the blood is consolidated and the qi is harmonized, will there be no illness entering from outside.[41p]

　　　　　乳哺

　　汤氏曰：小儿乳哺，须要得法。乳者奶也，哺者食也。乳后不得便与食，哺后不得便与乳。小儿脾胃怯弱，乳食相并，难以克化，周岁以上，必成乳癖食癖，于腹中作疼作热，疳病从此起也。　　凡乳母血气为乳汁也。五情善恶，悉血气所生，宜戒喜怒，一切禁忌。不可用孤臭、瘿瘘、气嗽病者，及身体疥癣、头疮发少、紧唇、耳聋、音哑、齆鼻、癎病等，方可用乳儿。　　夏中盛热时，乳母浴后或儿啼，不可与乳，能使儿成胃毒，秋成赤白痢。浴后可令定息良久，热退乳之，故无患也。　　聂氏曰：盛啼不可食乳。恐气逆不顺，聚而为(口逆)，亦能成惊风也。　　《千金》论曰：凡乳儿乳来多，猛取出挼后再乳。父母交合之间，儿卧于侧或惊起，不可乳儿，盖气乱未定，必能杀儿也。　　巢氏云：小儿啼未定，气息不调，母不可以乳饮儿。盖恐乳不得下，停滞胸膈，则为呕吐也。　　夜间乳儿，母起身坐，抱儿喂之。[42p]

Breastfeeding

Tang said: For infants, breastfeeding must be done properly. "Milk" refers to breast milk, and "feeding" refers to food. After breastfeeding, do not immediately offer solid food, and after feeding, do not immediately offer milk. Infants have weak spleen and stomach, and combining milk and food makes digestion difficult. After one year, this will lead to milk and food stagnation in the abdomen, causing pain and heat, and thus development of malnutrition.

Generally, the milk of a wet nurse is derived from her blood and energy. The emotions of joy and anger all arise from the blood and energy, so she should avoid strong emotions and all taboos. The nurse must not have conditions like foul body odor, goiter, cough, scabs, baldness, thick lips, deafness, hoarseness, nasal flaring, or epilepsy, as these may affect the infant negatively.

During hot summer months, after the wet nurse bathes or when the baby cries, do not offer milk, as it may lead to stomach toxins and cause dysentery in fall. After bathing, it is advisable to let the nurse rest for a long while until the heat dissipates before breastfeeding, thus avoiding problems.

Nie said: If the baby cries excessively, do not provide milk. This may cause disordered energy to rise, potentially leading to convulsions.

The "Thousand Gold" says: If the baby wants more milk, one should remove the baby, knead the breast, and then offer milk again. If parents are engaged in intimacy and the child is lying to the side or wakes up in surprise, do not offer breastfeeding, as the chaotic energy may harm the baby.

Cao said: If the baby is crying and breath not stable, the mother should not breastfeed. This is to avoid obstructing the flow of milk, which may lead to nausea.

At night, the mother should sit up to hold and feed the baby.[42p]

　　每侵早欲饮乳，皆须捏去宿乳。
　　乳汁勿投于地，虫蚁食之，令乳无汁，可沃东壁上佳。
　　　　　乳令儿病

　　喜乳，涎喘生惊。
　　孙兆云：令儿上气颠狂，亦令儿生痰喘急或生惊。　　怒乳，疝气腹胀。
　　《千金翼》云：怒乳令儿疝气。扁鹊云：女子则腹胀。　　寒乳，奶片不化。
　　华佗论云：乳气寒虚冷，故令便青而啼。《千金冀》云：令儿咳嗽。　　热乳，面黄不食。
　　《千金翼》云：令儿呕吐。张氏云：热乳伤损肺气，令儿龟胸。气乳，吐泻腹胀。　　《宝鉴》云：令儿面黄白，乳哺减少，夜啼哯乳。　　病乳，能生诸疾。
　　令儿黄瘦骨蒸，盗汗嗞煎夜哭。孙氏云：病乳则致虚羸及生诸疾。　　壅乳，吐逆生痰。[43p]

Every time one intends to drink milk in the morning, one must squeeze out the old milk.
Do not spill the milk on the ground, for insects and ants will consume it, leaving the milk devoid of substance, which can be used to nourish the good walls of the east.
Milk can cause the child to be ill.

Pleasant milk causes drooling and wheezing.
Sun Zhao says: It makes the child’s breath chaotic and can induce phlegm, wheezing, or even fright.
Angry milk causes hernia and abdominal distension.
The "Qianjin Yi" says: Angry milk leads to hernia in children. Bian Que says: For women, it causes abdominal swelling.
Cold milk causes the milk to curdle.
Hua Tuo notes: The cold milk causes weakness and crying. The "Qianjin Ji" states: It causes the child to cough.
Hot milk causes pallor and lack of appetite.
The "Qianjin Yi" states: Hot milk causes vomiting. Zhang notes: Hot milk injures lung qi, leading to a hunched chest in children.
Qi milk causes vomiting and diarrhea, as well as abdominal distension.
The "Baojian" states: It results in the child having a pale yellow complexion, reduced nursing, and nighttime crying due to hunger.
Sick milk can lead to various illnesses.
It makes the child yellow, emaciated, sweaty at night, and crying from discomfort. Sun’s commentary states: Sick milk results in weakness and causes various ailments.
Stagnant milk causes regurgitation and phlegm. [43p]

　　《灵秘》云：壅乳成痰涎，涎壅生惊。《宝鉴》云：壅乳成奶癖。又吐逆生痰。　　鬾乳，腹急脏冷。
　　《宝鉴》云：腹急而泻，胸背皆热，夜啼肌瘦，一如积块。　　醉乳，恍惚多惊。
　　《千金冀》云：令小儿热，腹急痛。扁鹊云：醉淫随乱乳儿，恍惚多惊。　　淫乳，必发惊癎。
　　《宝鉴》云：乳母淫佚情乱乳儿，令吐泻身热，啼叫如鸦，不治。　　已上乳，急欲乳儿，能生诸病，不可不忌也。凡喜怒气乱未定乳儿，则成吐泻腹痛，疳黄不食。寒热壅积不散乳儿，则成痰癖涎嗽，肺胀龟胸。醉淫喘乳，多发惊癎。《圣惠方》云：醉淫喘乳，能杀小儿。《圣济经》论：乳者夏不欲热，热致吐逆；冬不欲寒，寒则致下痢。母不欲怒，怒则令上气颠狂；母不欲醉，醉则令身热腹满。母方吐下而乳，则致虚羸；母有积热而乳，则变黄不能食。新房而乳，则瘦悴交胫不能行。大抵乳食不好，则生疾病。[44p]

The "Ling Mi" states: Congested milk turns into phlegm, which can cause fright. The "Bao Jian" mentions: Congested milk leads to a milk habit. Additionally, reverse flow can generate phlegm.

Feeding congested milk and inducing abdominal urgency can lead to internal chill. The "Bao Jian" also mentions that urgency and diarrhea arise, with heat in the chest and back, and nighttime crying and emaciation, akin to a stagnation lump.

Drunken milk can lead to confusion and excessive fright. The "Qian Jin Ji" states: If a child becomes hot with abdominal pain, according to Bian Que, drunken indulgence can cause confusion and excessive fright in infants.

Indulgent milk will surely result in fright and seizures. The "Bao Jian" states that a wet nurse's indulgence and emotional chaos can lead to vomiting, diarrhea, body heat, and crying like a crow—an untreated condition.

As for the aforementioned milk issues, they urgently affect infants and can lead to various illnesses, thus they should not be overlooked. In general, if there is emotional disturbance from joy or anger in the mother, the child will experience vomiting, diarrhea, abdominal pain, and failure to eat due to malnutrition. Accumulated cold and heat that does not disperse can cause phlegm, excess saliva, coughing, lung bloating, and a hardened chest. Drunken indulgence can lead to excessive fright and seizures in infants.

The "Sheng Hui Fang" notes that drunken breastfeeding can endanger a child. The "Sheng Ji Jing" discusses that milk should not be hot during summer; heat causes vomiting. In winter, it should not be cold; cold leads to diarrhea. A mother should avoid anger; anger results in upwards distress causing mania. A mother should avoid drunkenness; drunkenness leads to body heat and fullness in the abdomen. If the mother vomits or has diarrhea while breastfeeding, it can lead to weakness and emaciation; if she has accumulated heat while breastfeeding, it can turn yellow and lead to inability to eat. If breastfeeding occurs soon after marriage, the child may be weak and unable to walk. Generally, if breastfeeding or feeding is poor, it will lead to illness.[44p]

　　《宝鉴》云：儿五十日，可哺如枣核，百日弹丸，早晚二哺。莫抱檐下澡浴，当风解衣，哭未断而乳，冒冷而哺。又不可在神佛驴马畔，各房异户之亲，诸色物器，并不可触犯之，害子性为惊癎。经云：三岁未满，勿食鸡肉，子腹生虫。　　钱乙云：儿多因爱惜过当，三两岁犹未饮食，至脾胃虚弱，平生多病。半年，宜煎陈米稀粥、粥面时时与之。十月后，渐与稠粥烂饮，以助中气，自然易养少病。惟忌生冷油腻甜物等。　　《外台》崔氏初哺儿法，以平定成日丑寅辰巳酉日大吉。　　男忌戊己日，女忌丙丁日。[45p]

The "Baojian" states: At five days old, a child can be fed like a jujube pit; at a hundred days, like a bullet; feed twice daily, morning and evening. Do not bath the baby under eaves, undress in the wind, or nurse while he is still crying, as this can lead to cold exposure during feeding. Avoid being near spirits or animals, and do not touch various belongings of different families, as this might harm the child's nature and cause seizures. The classics state: Before reaching three years, do not feed chicken, as it leads to worms in the child's belly.

Qian Yi states: A child often suffers from excessive care. If they are still not eating well by two or three years, their spleen and stomach may become weak, leading to frequent illness. After six months, it is best to give them thin rice porridge and sometimes noodle soup. After ten months, gradually introduce thicker porridge to strengthen their energy and make them easier to raise with fewer illnesses. Avoid raw, cold, oily, and sweet foods.

According to the "Wai Tai," Cui's method for the initial feeding of children aligns with auspicious days such as the Day of the Earth or the Days of the Tiger, Rabbit, Dragon, Snake, and Rooster. Boys should avoid the days of Wu and Ji; girls should avoid the days of Bing and Ding.[45p]

　　　　　断乳法

　　小儿年至四五岁，当断乳而不肯断者，宜用　眉膏。断乳之后，方可渐与肉食，则无疳癖之患。
　　　　　杂将护法

　　张焕曰：乳母须每日三时，摸儿顶后风池。若壮热者，即须熨之使微汗，即愈。　　谚云：戒养小儿，谨护风池。风池在颈项筋两辕之边，有病乃治之。疾微切不可妄针灸，亦不用辄吐下。所以然者，针灸伤儿经络，吐下伤动脏腑故也。　　婴儿暑中，令在稍凉处，乳母勿禁新水，亦不宜多。　　婴儿春夏间有疾，不可乱有动下，使下焦虚，上焦热，变成大病也。　　婴儿须看禀受南北之殊，盖地生寒温不同故也。　　婴儿生后两满月，即目瞳子成，能笑识人。乳母不得令生人抱之，及不令见非常之物。[46p]

Weaning Method

When a child reaches the age of four or five and is reluctant to wean, it is advisable to use eyebrow balm. After weaning, one may gradually introduce meat into their diet, which will help prevent the risk of malnutrition.

Miscellaneous Care Methods

Zhang Huan said: The wet nurse should daily at three times touch the child's crown at the Fengchi point. If the child has a strong fever, one must apply compresses to induce slight sweating for recovery. It is said: "Be cautious in raising children, and carefully protect the Fengchi point." The Fengchi point is located at the side of the neck where the tendons meet; treat it only when there is illness. Do not recklessly employ acupuncture or other invasive methods, nor should one induce vomiting or diarrhea, as these can harm a child's meridians and disrupt their internal organs. During summer, keep the infant in a somewhat cool place; the wet nurse should not restrict them from drinking fresh water, but it should not be excessive. If an infant shows illness in spring or summer, one must avoid indiscriminate purging, as it may lead to deficiencies in the lower body and excess heat in the upper body, resulting in severe illness. Infants should be considered differently based on their geographic origins, as the temperature of the earth varies. After two full months of life, the infant’s eyes and smiles develop, and they can recognize people. The wet nurse must not allow strangers to hold the child, nor should the child be exposed to unusual objects.[46p]

　　婴儿百晬，任脉生，能反复。乳母当存节喜怒，适其寒温。　　婴儿半晬，尸骨已成。乳母当教儿学坐。　　婴儿二百日，外掌骨成。乳母教儿地上匍匐。　　婴儿三百日，膑骨成。乳母教儿独立。　　婴儿周晬，膝骨已成。乳母教儿行步。　　上件并是定法。盖世之人不能如法存节，往往抱儿过时，损伤筋骨，且宜戒之为吉。　　万全论云：田妇护儿，绝无他疾。譬之草木生深山大泽，容易合抱。至于异果奇材，纵加培养，间有不秀实者，岂贵贱异哉。数见风日，即血凝气刚，肌肉硬密，堪耐风寒，以田舍儿较之相似。[47p]

When an infant reaches a hundred days, the Ren Meridian develops, and they can react repeatedly. The wet nurse should manage her emotions of joy and anger and adapt to the child's temperature needs.

At half a year, the infant’s bones have formed. The wet nurse should teach the child how to sit.

At two hundred days, the external bones develop. The wet nurse should teach the child to crawl on the ground.

At three hundred days, the kneecap has formed. The wet nurse should teach the child to stand independently.

At one year, the knee bones have developed. The wet nurse should teach the child to walk.

All the above are established principles. If a person in the world cannot adhere to these guidelines, they often hold the child too long, damaging their muscles and bones; thus, it is advisable to refrain for good fortune.

The Treatise on Full Health states: A farmer's wife caring for her child should have no other ailments. This is akin to grass and trees growing in deep mountains and large marshes, easily able to be embraced. As for rare fruits and unique materials, even with cultivation, there are instances where they do not bear fruit; is their value or worth really different? When exposed to wind and sun, the blood solidifies, the vitality becomes strong, and the muscles grow firm and dense, able to withstand wind and cold, resembling children raised in rural areas.[47p]

　　　　　浴儿

　　儿生三日，以桑、榆、桃、柳各取嫩枝三寸长者二三十节煎汤，看冷热，入猪胆汁二三枚浴之。　　浴汤用猪胆、益母草，不生疮疥；用金、银、虎头骨、麝、丹砂，辟恶气客忤惊癎；用桃、梅、李、楮根，解体热温壮之病。须浴时煮。　　汤须不冷不热，于无风密室浴之，勿令久。　　浴讫，以粉摩之，或以光粉、蚌粉扑身，辟邪吉。　　纪用经浴法：寅卯酉日吉，壬午丁未癸已凶。不能上三日，勿犯下三日。　　儿初生以三日浴，或五日浴，七日浴，须选吉日。[48p]

Bathe the Infant

When a child is born, on the third day, take tender branches of mulberry, elm, peach, and willow, each around three inches long, and boil them to make a medicinal bath. Check the temperature, adding two or three pieces of pig bile for the bath. The bathing solution should contain pig bile and motherwort, which prevents sores and skin diseases; gold, silver, tiger bone, musk, and cinnabar to drive away evil spirits and prevent fright and convulsions; and roots from peach, plum, cherry, and other trees to alleviate heat and strength-related ailments. This must be boiled right before bathing.

The bathing solution should be neither too cold nor too hot, carried out in a windless, closed room. The bath should not last too long. After bathing, apply powder to the skin, or use bright powder and clam shell powder to ward off evil and bring good fortune.

According to the guidelines for bathing: the days of the tiger, rabbit, and rooster are auspicious, while the days of the water horse, fire goat, and earth chicken are inauspicious. You should not bathe on the third day following birth, nor should you bathe within three days before that. For a newborn, bathe on the third, fifth, or seventh day, selecting an auspicious date.[48p]

　　　　　断脐法

　　《宝鉴》论：断脐若用剪刀，先于怀中令暖。又水入脐、多天钓，痛苦啼叫，面青黑。脐伤动令久不干，伤外风即口噤不可救。
　　　　　灸脐法

　　《圣惠》云：儿生一宿，抱近明无风处，看脐上有赤脉直上者，即于脉尽头灸三壮，赤散无患矣。
　　　　　下胎毒法

　　张焕云：婴儿初生第一日，才断脐，绷袍讫，看儿形色，若面红润色赤，啼声响快者，宜用汞粉法，良久有脐粪便下为佳；次用甘草法；次用朱蜜法。临时更看形色，若面色多青白，啼声不响，即不须服。次用牛黄法。古方又有黄连法、非汁法、猪乳法等。在人看儿寒热怯壮，择所宜而用之尔。[49p]

Method for Cutting the Umbilical Cord

The "Precious Mirror" states: When cutting the cord, if using scissors, warm them first in your bosom. If water enters the cord, and the baby cries painfully while turning blue and black, it indicates a serious condition. If the cord wound does not dry for a long time, and external wind affects it, the mouth may become silent and the situation becomes uncontrollable.

Moxibustion of the Umbilical Cord

The "Holy Benefit" states: When a child is born and has spent one night, hold them close in a bright, windless place. If you notice a red vein running straight up from the umbilical area, apply moxibustion at the end of the vein three times, and the red will dissipate without issue.

Method for Treating Congenital Toxins

Zhang Huan says: On the first day after birth, once the cord is cut and the clothing is finished, observe the child's complexion. If the face is rosy and appears vibrant, and the cries are loud and quick, then apply mercury powder, as it is good for relieving any remaining cord remnants. Next, use licorice; then apply red honey. Continue to observe the complexion; if it appears more pale and blue, and the cries are weak, there is no need for medication. Next, you may use buffalo horn powder. Ancient prescriptions also include methods using Coptis, non-juice treatments, pig's milk, etc. When observing the child's cold/heat and strength, choose the appropriate method to use accordingly.[49p]

　　　　　藏胞衣法

　　崔氏云：儿衣清水洗，勿令沙土草污；又清酒洗之。仍内钱一文在衣中，盛新瓶内，青绵裹，瓶口密盖，置便宜处。三日后，依月吉地向阳高燥处，入地三尺埋之，瓶上土厚一尺七寸，须牢筑，今儿长寿智慧。若不谨，为猪狗食，令颠狂；虫蚁食，令病恶疮；犬鸟食，令兵死。近社庙，令见鬼；近深水污池，令溺死；近故灶，令惊惕；近井旁，令聋盲。弃道路街巷，令绝嗣；当门户，令声不出耳聋；着水流下，令青盲；弃火里，令生烂疮；着林木头，令自绞死。此忌须慎。　　每于天德月空处埋之。【正月天德在丁，月空在丙壬。余详官本历日。】 若遇反支，宜挂宅外福德上向阳高燥处，待过月，然后依法埋藏，吉。　　甲乙日生，丙丁日藏；丙丁日生，戊己日藏；戊己日生，庚辛日藏；庚辛日生，壬癸日藏，吉。[50p]

The Method of Preserving the Child's Clothing

Cui says: The child's clothing should be washed with clear water, ensuring it is not soiled by sand, dirt, or grass; then wash it again with clear wine. Place a coin inside the clothing, put it in a new jar, wrap it in green cotton, tightly seal the jar, and keep it in a suitable place. After three days, on an auspicious day of the month, bury it in a sunlit, high, and dry area, three feet deep, with at least one foot and seven inches of soil above the jar, sealed well. This will bring longevity and wisdom. If not careful, it may become food for pigs and dogs, leading to madness; if eaten by insects or ants, it may cause illnesses or sores; if eaten by dogs or birds, it may lead to death in war. Near a community shrine, it may cause visions of ghosts; near deep or dirty water, it may lead to drowning; near an old stove, it may cause fright; near a well, it may cause deafness or blindness. Abandoning it in roads or alleys may lead to the end of descendants; placing it at a doorway may cause silence or deafness; in flowing water may lead to green blindness; in fire may cause rotten sores; in trees may lead to self-hanging. These taboos must be observed with caution. Bury it during the time of Heavenly Virtue and the Void of the month. [In the first month, Heavenly Virtue is on Ding, and Void on Bing and Ren. For further details, refer to the official calendar.] If an opposing day occurs, it is better to hang it outside the house in a place of fortune, facing the sun in a high and dry area, and wait until the month has passed before proceeding to bury it according to the rules, which is auspicious. If born on a Jia or Yi day, bury it on Bing or Ding days; if born on Bing or Ding days, bury it on Wu or Ji days; if born on Wu or Ji days, bury it on Geng or Xin days; if born on Geng or Xin days, bury it on Ren or Gui days, which is auspicious.[50p]

　　　　　剃头法

　　《集验方》云：小儿初剃头，俱不择日，皆于满月日剃之。盖风俗所尚，前产妇未得出房，于满月即与儿俱出，谓胎发秽有触神灶，令小儿不安，故于此日必剃头而出。凡剃头就温暖避风处，及剃后须以杏仁三枚去皮尖研碎，入薄荷三叶，再同研，却入生麻油三四滴，腻粉拌和，头上擦以避风邪，免生疮疥热毒。其后小儿亦宜此法。[51p]

Head Shaving Method

In "Collected Verification Recipes," it states: For infants' first head shaving, no specific date is chosen; it is done on the full moon day. This is due to customary beliefs. After childbirth, women have not yet left the room, and on the full moon, they and their child both go out. It is believed that fetal hair is impure and can disturb the spiritual fires, causing the infant to be restless; therefore, shaving the head on this day is essential.

When shaving the head, it should be done in a warm place, avoiding the wind. After shaving, three peeled and crushed apricot kernels should be mixed with three leaves of mint, ground together, then added with three or four drops of raw sesame oil, combined with powder, and applied on the head to ward off wind and evil spirits, preventing sores, scabs, and heat toxins. This method is also suitable for the child thereafter.[51p]

　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

　　　　　初生裹脐

　　夫人之脐也，受生之初，父精母血，相受凝结，胞胎混沌，从太极未分之时，一气分得二六，穴中如产四穴，外通二肾，内长赤白二脉，四穴之中，分为表里，在母腹中母呼儿呼，母吸儿吸，是一身脐带，如花果在枝而通蒂也。一月一周，真气渐足。既产胎衣未脱，脐带且缓断。倘脐门未闭，感风伤寒，即损婴儿真气。遂以艾火熏蒸数次，则真气无患矣。凡初生时，用绵裹脐带，离肚二三寸处，以绵扎住，却于线外将脐带剪断；片时去线，待血流尽。看近肚处，脐有两小孔，一大孔；用鹅毛管送炼脐药一二分，入大孔内，以手指轻轻揉散，艾灸脐头三炷，结作扢搭，软帛腰裹，切不可时常揭看，待脐落去，自无风矣。又法：落胎之时，视其脐软者，不须治。如脐硬直者，定有脐风，急用银簪于脐根旁剌破一二处，入麝香未少许，艾灸三炷，极妙。[52p]

Introduction to Medicine
(Ming Dynasty - Li Chen)

On the Umbilicus of Newborns

The umbilicus of a person, at the time of birth, is formed by the mingling of the father’s essence and the mother’s blood. It comes together and solidifies, with the fetal body in a state of chaos. From the undifferentiated state of Taiji, the primordial qi separates into two and six (yin and yang). Inside the womb, there are four spaces that correspond with the two kidneys externally and two vessels—one red and one white—internally. Among these four spaces, there is division between surface and interior. Inside the mother’s belly, the mother breathes in and the baby breathes out; as the mother inhales, the baby inhales as well, forming a whole through the umbilical cord, just as flowers and fruits are connected through their stems.

One month after birth, the true qi gradually becomes sufficient. Once the placenta has been delivered, the umbilical cord is slowly cut. If the umbilical opening has not closed, exposure to wind or cold may harm the baby's true qi. Therefore, it is advisable to use mugwort to fumigate and steam multiple times, ensuring the true qi is protected. When a newborn is first handled, use cotton to wrap the umbilical cord, two to three inches away from the belly, securing it with cotton and then cutting the umbilical cord with thread outside the secured area; wait a moment for the blood to flow out completely.

Upon examining the area close to the belly, the umbilicus has two small holes and one large hole. Use a goose feather tube to introduce a small amount of umbilical medicine into the large hole, gently massaging it with a fingertip. Perform moxibustion on the umbilicus three times, then bind it with a soft cloth, ensuring it is not frequently uncovered. Allow the umbilicus to fall naturally, as this will prevent exposure to wind.

Additionally, when the placenta is expelled, if the umbilicus is soft, there is no need for treatment. However, if the umbilicus is hard and straight, it indicates umbilical wind. Quickly use a silver hairpin to prick one or two places near the umbilical root, then apply a small amount of musk and perform moxibustion three times, which is highly effective.[52p]

　　　　　藏胎衣

　　小儿胎衣，藏之宜生气方上。正月子方，二月丑，三寅四卯，五辰六巳，七午八未，九申十酉，十一戌十二亥方。如生气方有不便，依历日藏于奏书博士月德方上，忌月空三杀太岁方上。俗多置之河中者非。
　　　　　调护

　　养子须调护，看承莫纵弛。乳多终损胃，食壅即伤脾。被厚非为益，衣单正所宜。无风频见日，寒暑顺天时。初生三五月，宜绷缚令卧，勿竖头抱出，免致惊癎。六个月方可与稀粥，不可将乳同吃，令儿生疳积。五岁方可吃荤腥。
　　　　万病回春 【明　龚廷贤】

　　　　　初生

　　小儿初生，宜用七八十岁老人旧裙旧袄，改作小儿衣衫，真气相滋，令儿有寿。富贵之家，切不宜新制纻丝绫罗毡绒之类与小儿。不惟生疾，抑且折福，必致夭伤。[53p]

Concealing the Afterbirth

The afterbirth of a newborn should be buried in auspicious directions. It is best to do this in the first month during the proper timing: during the second month (Chou), the third month (Yin), the fourth month (Mao), the fifth month (Chen), the sixth month (Si), the seventh month (Wu), the eighth month (Wei), the ninth month (Shen), the tenth month (You), the eleventh month (Xu), and the twelfth month (Hai). If the auspicious direction is inconvenient, it should be buried according to the calendar in the direction of the Doctor of Writing on the moon’s virtue, avoiding directions ruled by emptiness, three killings, and the Grand Duke. It is improper to place it in the river.

Nurturing and Care

Raising a child requires careful nurturing; attention is necessary, and one must not be lax. Too much milk will damage the stomach, while obstructive foods will harm the spleen. Too thick clothing does not benefit; appropriate clothing should be light. Avoid wind and seek sunlight; maintain harmony with the seasons. In the first three to five months after birth, the infant should be swaddled and laid down, and should not be held upright to avoid startling fits. Only after six months can one offer thin porridge, avoiding mixing with milk to prevent sores. Meat may be introduced only after the age of five.

Restoration of Health

Upon birth, it is advisable to dress the newborn in old skirts and coats from elderly individuals aged seventy or eighty, transformed into baby clothes, as this helps nurture the vital energy and grants longevity. In wealthy families, it is crucial not to dress the child in new silk or brocade, as this could not only lead to illness but also diminish fortune, potentially resulting in untimely death.[53p]

　　　　小儿卫生总微论方【宋　撰人未详】　　宋　撰人未详　原作「明徐恒」，误。《小儿卫生总微论方》成书于宋高宗绍兴二十六（）年，不着撰人。明万历十四年（年）徐恒重修。
　　　　　洗浴论

　　儿才生下，须先洗浴，以荡涤污秽，然后可断脐也。若先断脐，则浴水入脐而为脐疮等病。及浴水须用药预先煎下，以瓶贮顿，临时旋暖用之，不犯生水，方佳。并已后浴之，亦用药煎汤，拣所宜时日，则大良矣。凡浴宜用寅卯百日。若初生不值，但于日中选此三时，如时亦不值，惟忌壬午丁巳癸巳日时大凶而与避之，余皆可也。　　用猪胆汁汤浴儿，则不患疮癣，皮肤滑泽。用金、银、虎骨、丹砂煎汤，则辟邪恶去惊；单用虎骨亦得。用李叶切半斤前汤，则解肌热，去温壮。用白芷二两、苦参三两挫碎煎汤，则去诸风。[54p]

On Bathing Infants

When a child is born, it is essential to bathe them first, to cleanse away impurities, and then the umbilical cord can be severed. If the cord is cut first, the bathwater may enter the navel, leading to conditions like navel sores. The bathing water must be prepared with medicinal herbs beforehand, stored in a bottle, and warmed up as needed, avoiding fresh water for the best results. Additionally, for subsequent baths, medicinal decoctions should also be used, choosing appropriate days and times, which is very beneficial. Generally, bathing should occur within the first hundred days during the hours of the Tiger and Rabbit. If the infant's first few days do not fall on these times, bathing can still be done at midday during three specific hours. It is crucial to avoid the days and times of Ren Wu, Ding Si, and Gui Si as they are greatly inauspicious. All other times are acceptable.

Using a pig bile broth for bathing infants prevents sores and skin conditions, making their skin smooth and moist. A decoction of gold, silver, tiger bone, and cinnabar repels evil spirits and calms fears; using only tiger bone is also sufficient. A mixture of half a pound of sliced plum leaves helps to disperse muscular heat and alleviate excess warmth. A decoction made of two taels of Bai Zhi and three taels of Ku Shen, crushed and boiled, can dispel all kinds of wind ailments.[54p]

用朔藋、葱白、胡麻叶、白芷、槁本、蛇床子煎汤，退热。用苦参、黄连、猪胆、白芨、杉叶、柏叶、枫叶煎汤，去风。用大麻仁、零陵香、丁香、桑葚、藁本煎汤，治诸疮。用金、银，桃奴、雄黄、丹砂煎汤，则辟邪除惊。用益母草煎汤，治疥疮诸疮。　　凡煎汤每用水一斗，入药煎至七升，去滓，通寒温用之。冬不可太热，夏不可令冷，须调停得宜，乃可用之。儿自生之后，须依时洗浴，以去垢污，又不可数数。若都不洗浴，则皮皴毛落，多生疮疥。凡洗浴时，于背上则微微少用水，余处任意。既不可极淋其背，亦不可久坐水中，则引惊作病，切须慎之！如常能依法用之，令儿体滑舒畅，血脉通流，及长少病，无不验也。[55p]

Use raw rice chaff, green onions, sesame leaves, angelica, dry roots, and chenopodium to brew a decoction to reduce fever. Use苦参 (ku shen),黄连 (huang lian), pig bile, white atractylodes, cypress leaves, cedar leaves, and maple leaves to brew a decoction to dispel wind. Use hemp seeds, ligusticum, cloves, mulberries, and dry roots to brew a decoction to treat various sores. Use gold, silver, peach branches, realgar, and cinnabar to brew a decoction to exorcise evil and dispel fright. Use motherwort to brew a decoction to treat scabies and other sores.

For each decoction, use one dou (approximately 10 liters) of water, boil the herbs until reduced to seven sheng (approximately 1.5 liters), strain out the dregs, and apply according to cold or warm conditions. In winter, do not make it too hot; in summer, do not let it be too cold; it must be adjusted properly before use.

After childbirth, a child must be bathed regularly to remove dirt, but not excessively. If bathing is neglected, the skin will become rough, hair will fall out, and sores or scabies may develop. During bathing, use a little water on the back and allow more on other areas. Do not overly soak the back, nor let the child sit in water for too long, as it may induce fright and illness; care must be taken! If these methods are properly followed, the child will have a smooth and comfortable body, good circulation, and be less prone to illness as they grow up, with evident results.[55p]

　　　　　断脐论

　　儿生下，须当以时断脐。若不以时断脐者，则令脐汁不干而生寒，为脐风之由。其断脐带当令长至足趺，或云当长六寸。若太短则伤脏，令儿腹中不调；若太长则伤肌，令儿皮枯鳞起。才断脐讫，须用烙脐饼子，安脐带上，烧三壮，炷如麦大，若儿未啼，灸至五七壮。灸了，上用封脐散封裹之。法须捶治帛子令柔软，用方四寸许，上置新绵厚半寸，及上置药末，适紧慢以封之。如不备其药，即用极细熟艾一块，置于上封之。但不令封帛紧急，急则令儿吐哯。又须常切照顾，勿令湿着及襁绷中，亦不可令儿尿湿，恐生疮肿及引风也。[56p]

Discussion on Cutting the Umbilical Cord

When a child is born, the umbilical cord must be cut at the proper time. If it is not cut in time, the cord juice remains, leading to coldness, which causes umbilical wind. The cord should be cut to a length that reaches the ankle, or about six inches. If it is too short, it can harm the organs, causing imbalance in the child's abdomen; if too long, it can harm the flesh, causing the child's skin to become dry and scaly. Immediately after cutting the cord, one must use a cord moxibustion cake, placing it over the cord stump and burning it three times, with each treatment about the size of a grain of wheat. If the child has not cried, apply moxibustion five to seven times. After the moxibustion, one should seal the cord stump with a cord seal powder. The fabric used should be beaten to make it soft, about four inches square, with a layer of new cotton half an inch thick placed on top, and medication powder sprinkled on, properly tightening and sealing it. If the necessary medicine is not on hand, a finely ground piece of cooked mugwort may also be used for sealing. However, the cloth should not be sealed too tightly, as this may cause the child to vomit. Additionally, constant care is required to ensure it does not get wet or contact the swaddling cloth, and the child’s urine must not wet it, as this could lead to sores, swelling, or attract wind.[56p]

　　《圣济经》云：凡儿初生恶血未纳者，拭以绵指；吞而在胷膈者吐。以甘草；入而在腹内者利，以黄连末粉。皆所以革污秽也。次用好朱砂一大豆许，细研水飞，炼蜜一蚬壳，看稀稠和膏，分三剂，每用一剂，乳汁化，时时滴儿口中，三日内服尽即止。姚和众云：成炼朱砂能温肠胃，壮血气也。一日只可一豆许，分三次用，勿得过也。次用真牛黄一大豆许，细研，以炼蜜酸枣大，和成膏，每用一大豆许，乳汁化下，时时滴儿口中。姚和众云：能去惊，辟邪恶之气。若儿形色不实，怯弱者，不宜服之。如胎热或体色赤黄者，宜多服。此法在三日外也。[57p]

The "Sengji Jing" states: When a child is born and has not absorbed the unhealthy blood, it should be wiped with cotton and if it is swallowed and remains in the chest, induce vomiting. Use licorice for this purpose. If it has entered the abdomen, use a powder of Coptis to induce a purge. These are all methods to cleanse impurities. Next, take about a bean-sized quantity of good vermilion, finely ground and dissolved in water, and mixed with honey from a clam shell, adjusting the thickness to form a paste. Divide this into three doses, administering one dose at a time by mixing it with breast milk and dropping it into the child's mouth. Complete the doses within three days. Yao He and others say that prepared vermilion can warm the intestines and stomach, and invigorate blood and qi. Only one bean-sized dose is allowed per day, divided into three times; do not exceed this. Then use genuine ox gall, about the size of a bean, finely ground and prepared with honey to the size of a sour jujube, forming a paste. Each time, use a large bean-sized amount, dissolved in breast milk and dropped into the child’s mouth. Yao He and others say it can dispel fright and eliminate malevolent energy. However, if the child's appearance is weak or frail, it should not be administered. If the child shows signs of heat or has a red or yellow complexion, it should be taken more frequently. This method is applicable for a duration of three days.[57p]

　　　　　慎护论

　　凡乳母慎护养儿，乳哺欲其有节，襁褓欲其有宜，达其饥饱，察其强弱，通其浓薄，循其寒燠，盖自有道，不可不知也。　　凡儿自初生至满月，常取猪乳滴儿口中。又以珍珠末一大豆许，用蜜一蚬壳和之，分三次或四次，每十日内外，与一次涂儿口中。安心神，镇魂魄。　　凡儿于春时，不可覆头裹足，致阳气不得出泄，则发热矣。
　　　　　食忌论

　　凡小儿有不可食之物，不可不知，今具于后。　　小儿不可多食栗子，令儿气弱行迟，热食则气滞。　　小儿不可食蕨菜，令儿立则无力，久不能行。　　小儿不可食芡，令儿不能行。
　　小儿不可食黍米、鸡肉、胡瓜，令儿腹中生虫。　　小儿不可食越瓜，令儿发痼疾。
　　小儿不可食荞麦，令儿发落。
　　小儿不可食(艹鳬)茨，令儿挤下痛。　　小儿不可食鲟鱼，令儿生症癖。[58p]

On Cautious Nurturing

When a wet nurse carefully nurtures a child, she should breastfeed with moderation, wrap the child appropriately, ensure the child’s hunger and fullness are addressed, observe the child’s strength and weakness, adjust the thickness of nourishment, and respond to temperature changes. These practices are based on established principles that should not be overlooked. From birth until a month old, it is customary to administer a few drops of pig's milk into the infant's mouth. Additionally, take a large soybean's worth of powdered pearl, mix it with honey from a clam shell, and apply it to the child’s mouth in three or four doses, once every ten days or so. This calms the mind and stabilizes the spirit. During spring, infants should not have their heads and feet covered, as this would prevent the release of yang energy, leading to fever.

On Dietary Restrictions

There are certain foods that are unsuitable for young children; it is essential to be aware of these. Children should not eat too many chestnuts, as this weakens their qi and slows their movements; heated foods can cause qi stagnation. Children should not consume bracken fern, as it weakens their legs and prevents them from walking. They should not eat spiny water lily, as this hinders locomotion. Children should avoid millet, chicken, and cucumbers, as these can cause intestinal parasites. They should not eat pitcher plants, as this can lead to chronic ailments. Buckwheat should also be avoided, as it can cause hair loss. Children should not eat cocklebur, as it can result in pain during excretion. Lastly, they should not consume sturgeon, as this can induce disorders and obsessions.[58p]

　　小儿不可食炒豆猪肉，令儿生气壅致死。
　　　　活幼精要 【明　董凤翀】

　　　　　食忌论

　　大凡小儿，不宜多食。心之有病，不宜食咸。肺之有病，不宜食苦。肝之有病，忌食辛辣。脾之有病，忌食馊酸。肾之有病，忌饮甘甜。生葱与蜜，共食害人。苋菜鳖肉，共食生毒。鱼虾油腻，肺病忌食。生冷鸡卵，脾病忌食。鸡羊煎炒，心病忌食。葱蒜油面，肝病忌食。腰子肚肺，心血葫荽，有病无病，俱不可食。飞禽瓦雀，食生疮疥。螺蛳蟹鮝，食生泻利。食甜成疳，食饱伤气。食冷成积，食酸损志。食苦耗神，食咸闭气。食肥生痰，食辣伤肺。莲子芡实，能通心气，石榴酸柑，大濇肠胃。干柿煮蔗，犹能益肺。蒸藕炒豆，于肝宜利。五味淮枣，脾家可意。食味淡薄，脏腑清气。爱子惜儿，须知禁忌。丁奚哺露，疾作无辜。救疗无门，悔之不及。育子之家，当为留意！[59p]

Children should not eat fried beans and pork, as it can cause anger and lead to death.

In general, children should not eat excessively. If there is a heart ailment, they should avoid salty foods. If there is a lung condition, they should steer clear of bitter foods. If there is a liver issue, spicy foods should be avoided. If the spleen is unwell, sour and spoiled foods should be excluded. If there is kidney trouble, sweet drinks are to be avoided. Green onions and honey, when consumed together, are harmful. Amaranth and turtle meat, together, produce toxins. Oily fish and shrimp are to be avoided in the case of lung diseases. Raw cold eggs should not be eaten if there are spleen issues. Fried chicken and lamb are not suitable for heart ailments. Green onions, garlic, and oily noodles must be avoided for liver diseases. Kidneys, stomachs, and lung parts, regardless of whether one is ill or not, should not be eaten. Birds and sparrows can cause sores and scabs when consumed. Snails and crabs can lead to severe digestive issues. Eating sweet food leads to illness, and eating too much can exhaust energy. Cold food can cause stagnation, and sour food can damage willpower. Bitter food can drain energy, and salty food can cause difficulty in breathing. Fatty food generates phlegm, and spicy food harms the lungs. Lotus seeds and water caltrops can help invigorate heart energy; pomegranates and sour oranges can greatly harm the intestines and stomach. Dried persimmons boiled with sugar can still benefit the lungs. Steamed lotus root and fried beans are good for the liver. Five-flavor jujubes can please the spleen. A bland diet is beneficial for the organs and promotes clear energy. Parents who love and cherish their children must be aware of these prohibitions. If overlooked, diseases can arise innocently. Once healing is needed, it may be too late for regrets. Families raising children should pay attention![59p]

　　　　景岳全书 【明　张介宾】

　　　　　儿初生

　　凡小儿初诞，宜以甘草细切少许，用沸汤泡汁，以淡为妙，不宜太甜。乃用软帛蘸汁，遍拭口中，去其秽浊。随用胡桃肉去皮嚼极烂，以稀绢或薄纱，包如小枣，内儿口中，使吮其汁，非独和中，且能养脏，最佳法也。若母气素寒，小儿清弱者，只以淡姜汤拭口，最能去胃寒，通神明，并可免吐泻之患。此法最妙，人所未知也。拭后用核桃法如前。　　一法：以牛黄半分，同朱砂研匀，蜜调，如前与吮为佳。[60p]

The Complete Book of Jingyue (Ming Dynasty, Zhang Jieben)

On the Birth of Infants

When an infant is born, one should take a small amount of finely chopped licorice and steep it in boiling water to make a mild solution, not too sweet. Use soft cloth to dab the solution, cleaning the mouth to remove impurities. Next, take walnut meat, peel it, and chew it thoroughly; then wrap it in thin silk or gauze, forming it like a small date, and place it in the infant's mouth so that it can suck the juice. This not only harmonizes the stomach but also nourishes the organs—it is the best method. If the mother has a cold constitution and the infant is weak and clear, simply use a mild ginger tea to clean the mouth, which is most effective for removing stomach cold, clarifying the mind, and can also prevent vomiting and diarrhea. This method is excellent and not widely known. After cleaning, follow the walnut method as mentioned earlier.

Another method: take half a portion of cow bile, mix it with cinnabar, and adjust it with honey as before for sucking.[60p]

极能辟痰，去秽恶，除热安神。然必母气多热，小儿肥盛者可用，清弱者不宜用。　　一古法拭口多有用黄连者，不知黄连大寒大苦，而小儿以胃气为主，安得初生即可以苦劣之气相犯，致损胃气，则他日变呕变泻，由此而起矣，大非所宜。　　一古法多用朱砂开口者。按陈文中曰：小儿初生，便服朱砂、轻粉、白蜜、黄连，本欲下胎毒，不知此皆伤脾败阳之药。轻粉下痰损心，朱砂下涎损神。儿实者服之软弱，弱者服之易伤，反致变生诸病，是故不可不察也。
　　　　东医宝鉴 【朝鲜　徐浚】
　　朝鲜　徐浚　原缺。《东医宝鉴》为朝鲜　徐浚等人撰，成书于明万历三十九年（年）。[61p]

It is extremely effective in dispersing phlegm, eliminating filth and evil, and calming the spirit. However, it should only be used when the child has excessive heat from maternal qi; it is not suitable for those who are weak and feeble.

In ancient practices, there was much use of Huanglian, but it is important to note that Huanglian is extremely cold and bitter, and since young children have their primary energy in the stomach, how can they be expected to withstand the detrimental effects of such bitterness immediately after birth? This could damage their stomach qi, leading to vomiting or diarrhea in the future, which is certainly not advisable.

Another ancient method often employed was grinding cinnabar to open the mouth. In medical texts, it is noted that newborns should take cinnabar, light powder, white honey, and Huanglian to clear fetal toxins; however, these are all substances that harm the spleen and damage yang. The light powder causes phlegm that weakens the heart, and cinnabar damages the spirit by lowering saliva. Strong children may process these substances too easily, while weak ones are easily harmed, resulting in various diseases. Therefore, careful consideration is crucial.[61p]

　　　　　保护法

　　《良方》曰：夜间不得令儿枕臂，须作一二豆袋，令儿枕，兼左右附之，可近乳母之侧。盖覆衣衾，须露儿头面。若一向仰卧，恐成惊痰，须时时回动之。
　　　　方

　　平和饮子 【《颅顖经》】　儿初生日与饮。《指迷》云：儿生三日后，与母服。　　人参　茯苓　甘草　升麻各二钱五分　　水一盏，煎一合半，时时与之。乳母忌油腻满月及百晬。如时冷加白朮，热加硝，各半钱。
　　百寿散海藏方　小儿初生未满月已前用之者，老无疮疥。　　黄连一两　朱砂一钱
