　　右水煎，令老母拭去口涎，净灌下。余药倾盆中浴儿，遍身搽妙。
　　浴体汤 【《小儿直诀》】
　　青黛三钱　天麻二钱　乌梢肉酒浸焙末，三钱　蝎尾去毒炒　朱砂研，各半钱　白矾三钱　麝香一钱　　右七味同研匀，每用三钱，水三碗，桃枝一握，并叶五七枚，同煎十沸，温热得所浴之。勿浴背上。[62p]

Protection Law

"The Good Formula" states: At night, do not let the child rest on an arm. One should make one or two bean bags for the child to rest upon, placing them on either side, close to the wet nurse. The clothes and blankets should cover the child, with the head and face exposed. If the child continuously lies on their back, they may be at risk of developing a startle reflex; therefore, they should be turned regularly.

Formula

Gentle Drink for Children (from the "Crane's Head Classic"): In the first few days after birth, a drink should be given. "Finger Guide" states: On the third day after birth, the mother should take it. Ingredients: Ginseng, Poria, Licorice, and Cimicifuga, each 2.5 grams, with one cup of water, boil down to 1.5 cups, and give it to the child from time to time. The wet nurse should avoid oily foods for a month after childbirth and during the hundred days. If it is cold, add half a portion of Atractylodes; if it is hot, add half a portion of Niter.

Hundred Longevity Powder, Sea Hidden Recipe: This is used for infants under one month, preventing sores and scabies. Ingredients: Huanglian (Coptis), 30 grams; Zhushā (Cinnabar), 3 grams.

Prepare by boiling with water, allowing the elder mother to wipe away drool and administer it cleanly. The remaining medicine should be used to bathe the child, applying it all over the body.

Bathing Body Decoction (from the "Classic of Young Children"):
Ingredients: Qīngdài (Indigo), 9 grams; Tiānmá (Gastrodia), 6 grams; Wūshāo (Caterpillar fungus) soaked and roasted powder, 9 grams; Scorpion tail (toxic parts removed and roasted), Zhushā (Cinnabar) ground, each 3 grams; Bái fán (Alum), 9 grams; Shèxiāng (Musk), 1 gram.

Mix the seven ingredients evenly. Use 9 grams of the mixture with three bowls of water, along with a handful of peach twigs and 5-7 leaves, boil until it reaches a warm temperature for bathing. Do not bathe the back.[62p]

Shen Xiong Pill
Rhubarb and Scutellaria, each 2 qian; Talc and Black Morning Glory, each 4 qian; Coptis, Mint, and Chuanqiong, each 5 fen. Grind these into a powder, make pills the size of a tung seed. Take 5 to 7 pills with warm water, adjusting dosage according to the child's size.

Yiyuan Powder
Talc 6 qian, Licorice 1 qian, Cinnabar a small amount. Grind these into a fine powder, taking 3 fen, mixed with honey and fresh water.

Detoxification and Longevity Ointment (from "The Secret of Infant Care") Treats newborns by wiping away harmful substances in the mouth. Within three days, apply this medicine to the child's mouth to detoxify and also prevent sores, rashes, and convulsions. Take 1 to 2 inches of the child's umbilical cord from the afterbirth, finely ground with new tile for 5 fen, 2.5 fen of Coptis powder, and 1 fen of Cinnabar powder. Mix these with honey and apply to the child's mouth within three days after birth to detoxify from fetal toxins.

Poria Pill (from "One Hundred Questions of Infants") Treats newborns who cannot cry. Quickly wipe their mouth to remove stagnant blood. If they cannot swallow, there will be no other illness. If delayed and harmful substances enter the abdomen, it may cause fullness and shortness of breath, preventing them from drinking milk; or if the child is cold while in the womb, it may cause abdominal pain and inability to breastfeed—this pill is recommended.

Medical Case:

In the "Complete Book of Jingyue," it is noted: My younger child was born in the Ding-si year, at the Yan estate, around the time of the White Dew festival, just over half a cycle of the moon. I noticed the new cool days ahead, and worried that the thin bedding might expose the child to cold air, sternly advising the caretakers to keep the child warm, but they did not take it seriously. A few days later, the child indeed began to have severe vomiting and diarrhea. I first used warming and spleen-harmonizing medicines, but to no avail. I then tried regulating formulas, yet they also did not work. After three days, I added three qian of ginseng, along with ginger, cassia, wuzhu, and nutmeg, still without effect. By the fourth day, the child was vomiting and diarrhea simultaneously, expelling half of what was consumed, with nothing retained in the belly. I had no choice but to use five or six qian of ginseng, along with one or two qian of aconite, ginger, cassia, etc. But even upon swallowing, the child would immediately vomit, leaving not a drop behind, and the milk expelled was clean and untainted, resembling milk still. At that time, the signs of danger in the child's condition were exceedingly grave, with no chance of recovery left.[73p]

余静坐默测其故，且度其寒气犯胃，而吐泻不止，若舍参、姜、桂、附之属，尚何术焉？伎止此，窘甚。忽于夜半而思意起，谓其胃虚已极，但药之气味略有不投，则胃不能受，随拒而出，矧附子味咸，亦能致呕，必其故也。因自度气味，酌其所宜，似必得甘辣可口之药，庶乎胃气可安，尚有生意。乃用胡椒三钱捣碎，加煨姜一两，用水二锺，煎至八分，另盛听用。又用人参二两，亦用水二锺，煎至一锺，另盛听用。用此二者，取其气味之甘辛纯正也。乃用茶匙挑合二者，以配其味。凡用参汤之十，加椒姜汤之一，其味微甘而辣，正得可口之宜。[74p]

I sat quietly, reflecting on the cause of the issue, considering that the cold energy was affecting the stomach, leading to endless vomiting and diarrhea. If I were to abandon herbs like ginseng, ginger, cinnamon, and aconite, what other methods could there be? The situation became dire. Suddenly, in the middle of the night, I had a thought: the stomach's deficiency had reached its limit, and if the medicine’s flavor was even slightly incompatible, the stomach would reject it. Moreover, since aconite has a salty flavor, it can also induce vomiting; this must be a contributing factor.

So I assessed the flavors and determined it was necessary to use a sweet and spicy remedy, as this would likely soothe the stomach energy and maintain vitality. I decided to use three qian of pepper, crushed, along with one liang of ginger, boiled in two zhongs of water until reduced by a third, and set aside for use. I also took two liang of ginseng, boiled in another two zhongs of water until reduced to one zhong, and set that aside as well.

With these two components, I aimed for a balanced flavor profile that was sweet and spicy. I combined the two, adjusting their taste with a teaspoon. For every ten doses of ginseng broth, I added one dose of the pepper and ginger broth, creating a mildly sweet and spicy flavor that was truly palatable.[74p]

遂温置热汤中，徐徐挑而与之，陆续渐进，经一时许，皆咽而不吐，竟得获效。自后乳药皆安，但泻仍未止也。自四鼓服起，至午未间，已尽二两之参。参尽后，忽尔躁扰呻吟，烦剧之甚。家人皆怨，谓以婴儿娇嫩脏腑，何堪此等热药，是必烧断肚肠也。相与抱泣。余虽疑之而不为乱，仍凝神熟思，意此药自四鼓至此，果药难堪，何于午前相安而此时遽变若此？其必数日不食，胃气新复，而仓廪空虚，饥甚则然也。傍有预备之粥，取以示之，则张皇欲得，其状甚急。乃与一小盏，辄鲸吞虎噬，又望其余；遂复与半碗，犹然不足；又与半碗，遂寂然安卧矣。[75p]

He then put it in warm soup, gradually spooning it to him, and slowly progressed. After a while, he swallowed it without spitting it out, and it turned out to be effective. From then on, the milk medicine was fine, but the diarrhea had still not stopped. From the fourth watch after taking it until noon, he had consumed two taels of ginseng. After the ginseng was finished, he suddenly became restless and moaned intensely. The family members complained, saying that with such tender bowels as a baby, how could he endure such hot medicine? It would definitely burn his intestines. They all wept together. Although I doubted, I did not panic, but still focused and thought deeply, considering that from the fourth watch until now, if the medicine was difficult to endure, why was he fine before noon and suddenly changed like this? It must be that after several days without food, his stomach was freshly restored, and with an empty belly, he would feel quite hungry. Nearby, there was some prepared porridge, and when I offered it to him, he became anxious and eagerly wanted it. He quickly gulped it down and looked for more. So I gave him a small bowl, and he devoured it like a whale swallowing and a tiger biting. Still not satisfied, I gave him half a bowl, yet it was still insufficient; so I gave him another half bowl, and then he quietly settled down to sleep.[75p]

至次日，复加制附，始得泻止全愈。呜呼！此儿之重生，固有天命，然原其所致之因，则人之脏气皆系于背，褥薄夜寒则寒从背俞而入，内干于脏，中必深矣。原其所治之法，用药虽当，而气味不投，无以相入，求救难矣。及其因饥发躁，使非神悟其机，倘妄用清凉一解，则全功尽弃，害可言哉！故余笔此以见病源之轻重，气味之相关，及诊治之活变，有如此关系者。虽然，此特以己之儿，故可信心救疗如是。设以他人之子，同有是病者，于用参数钱之时，见其未效，不知药未及病，必且烦言吠起，谤其误治，改用苦寒，无不即死，而仍归罪于用参者，此时黑白，将焉辨之？故再赘其详，用以广人之闻见云。
[76p]

The next day, I added more prescriptions, and only then did he begin to improve and fully recover. Alas! The rebirth of this child is indeed due to fate, but when considering the causes, it is evident that the internal heat of a person's organs is linked to the back. When the mattress is thin and the nights are cold, the chill enters through the back, deeply affecting the internal organs. The treatment method, although the medication is appropriate, lacks the proper essence and flavor to integrate; thus, seeking relief becomes difficult.

Additionally, when hunger causes restlessness, if the spirit does not recognize its condition, and one carelessly uses cooling remedies to resolve it, then all efforts may be in vain, causing further harm! Therefore, I write this to highlight the severity of the illness, the relationship of essences and flavors, and the dynamic nature of diagnosis and treatment. Although this is specific to my own child, it underscores the confidence in healing.

If another’s child suffers similarly and the prescribed treatments do not yield results, one might assume the medicine is misapplied and hastily criticize the treatment, switching to harsh, cold remedies, which could be fatal. Yet the blame would still fall on the use of ginseng. At such a time, how can one distinguish right from wrong? Thus, I elaborate on these details to broaden people's understanding and awareness.[76p]
